when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些事 , 但真正的事情是 , 未來將會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , alanturing , 在1936年 , 然後又發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全理論化了 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都從數學的觀點出發 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他奠定了數學在電腦科學上的基礎 , 說: 「 你怎麼把電腦創造出來的並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣是純機械的 , 或是像現在電腦一樣的電子化 , 又或者是未來的細胞 , 或是再說一次是機械化的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米技術 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器只要把它做得很小 , 所有的東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上有某種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂 」 的論點 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你看到一個連結 , 你說這東西是babbage建造的 , 真的是一部電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦做的所有事 , 只有很緩慢的速度 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓大家了解有多慢 , 它大約有1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 原本被放進去的 , 跑得比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一個ram打包機 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加入很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 我們今天在哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞士 , 科學博物館的檔案館 , 有成百上千頁的計劃和上千頁的筆記 , 是由charlesbabbage寫的 , 內容是關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計畫被我們稱之為計劃28這也是我與doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字他是科學博物館的計算機負責人同時也是開車這個計劃要建造出差異引擎的人我們的計劃就是把它做好
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	專案有許多部分可供使用 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二個是研究所有計劃的成果 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是一個模擬那機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部份是到科學博物館去建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為 , 與其在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作的聲響 。 大概我聞到了它運作的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫的 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎的存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過 , 因為他總是在擺弄新的計畫 , 但是當它真的在1940年代被打造出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我先讓各位稍微了解一下它的動作和影片 , 這僅僅顯示cpu運作的機械原理之一 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪它準備做加法 。 這是加法的運作原理所以你想像這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年之前 , 我們將有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場以影像呈現的演說中 , 雅曼•亞伯特蘭展示了他三個最近的人類計畫 , 我們的棲息地拍攝了他的系列作品《從天而降》中的空拍攝了他的作品《從天而降的地球人物》個人訪談 , 在他的網上作《六十億人》中 , 他的即將推出電影《家》中 , 透過拍攝的影片 , 記錄了人類對於環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南亞瑟•亞伯特把脆弱的地球限制從寬角度捕捉到 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球造成很大的影響 , 可以搭乘飛機來這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩隻大象的重量
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態問題我在這裡所排放的二氧化碳量相當於一個法國人一年內所排放的二氧化碳量
so what do i have to do ?	那我要怎麼辦呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺死一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵消我的碳 , 就像我每次都這麼做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是要呈現出我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我會給你們看一些例子 , 展示我在去年所拍攝的最後一張照片 。

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們工作不間斷 , 每七個小時就花24小時 , 來盡量提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂並不是個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量 , 是每年發現的三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新喀里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	由於全球暖化 , 珊瑚群的100%可能在2050年前就消失殆盡 。

our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命和地球的福祉息息相關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依靠水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	漁業、繁殖、農業 , 到現在都還是人類最重要的職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們緊密結合在一起的 , 遠大於將我們分裂的因素 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的天賦有著相同的需求 , 希望能超越自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而我們卻繼續在舉起牆壁讓自己分離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 遠超過整個人類歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林都消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源用量低 ,
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集養殖業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	只在嘗試改善我們的生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但貧富差距擴大了
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們正以比地球所能持續的速度快速許多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今可行的解決方案 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演說中 , 理查.resnick的演說顯示出便宜又快速的基因定序將會如何將健康照護顛倒過來 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我為大家介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上方
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 , 當然 , 還有y染色體的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	<unk>小男孩 , <unk>不好意思是 , 小男孩會讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 會看到雙螺旋結構生命的編碼是由這四個生化字母拼成的 , 我們稱之為基對 , 沒錯 , 是a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組有多少存在 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便亂丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但 , 事實上 , 如果我在這1280年的每一個像素上都放一個基對 , 乘以800個解析度螢幕 , 我們需要3000塊螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的是很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為其尺寸 , 一群人順便一提 , 有y染色體的人決定想要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 事實上 , 15年後 , 還有約40億美元 , 基因組序列完整並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最終的版本發表 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每根基底的成本大約是一美元 , 這是非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們把一個基因組複製50份然後把這些複製品全部切成50基對接著我們就進行大量並行地排序
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後把這些帶入軟體中 , 重新組合 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓你們對這看起來像什麼 , 人類基因組計劃:3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	每週可以做2000億基對 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 600年的變化將達到600年 , 這種步調緩慢沒有任何跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基對排序的代價 , 已經降低了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年給汽車加油的錢 , 一直等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星又開回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 電腦普及 , 醫學文獻的存檔 , 摩爾定律 , 舊式的定序方法 , 而這邊是所有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數刻度 , 你通常不會看到像那樣上升的線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以全世界對人類基因組的測序能力在今年大約有5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	根據被放置的機器 , 我們知道這點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	在可預見的未來裏每年這個數字都會翻一倍、三倍 , 甚至四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室佔據了所有容量的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人是絕對贏得這場新月球的競賽順帶一提
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人已經37歲了
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她提出了 「 階段二 」 雌激素受阻體陽性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術 , 化療和放射性治療
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又發現了第三個卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲又回來了 , 帶著更多的卵巢癌 , 做更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入了呼吸衰竭 , 8天後就會死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 這位女士在短短的10年內 , 會像放血一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因組研究所的同事rickwilson決定要研究一下這位女士的後遺傳人員
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他依序排序 , 帶著皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 及帶癌的骨髓 , 將兩者的基因組進行排序 , 只花了幾週的時間 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他在軟體中比較了這兩組基因組 , 他發現 , 其中之一 , 是一份刪除 , 橫跨30億個鹼基的兩千個鹼基 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因上有這種具有殺傷力的突變基因 , 你一生中就有百分之九十的機率會得癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這並沒有對這位女士有幫助 , 但這位女士有嚴重、深遠的影響 , 如果你願意 , 就會影響到她的家庭 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我是說 , 如果他們有相同的突變基因測試 , 他們會得到相同的基因測試 , 然後他們可以去做定期的篩檢 , 可以及早發現癌症 , 並且很有可能可以活得更久 , 更久更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我向各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出大腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信這些症狀並不搭配 , 透過一些英勇的努力 , 和很多的網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們擁有的是多巴反應式的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	他們得到了左旋多巴 , 症狀的確有改善 , 但沒有完全改善 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	原來這張圖片的這位先生是一位名叫joebeery的先生 , 他很幸運地是一家名為 " 生命科技 " 的公司的首見 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造大量全基因組測序工具的其中一間公司 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子接受定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們在一個叫做spr的基因上發現一系列突變 , 負責產生的血清素 , 和其他的基因中發現的 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給這些孩子使用了血清素前的藥物 , 現在他們非常正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有全基因組測序是不可能發生的 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前--這要花費10萬美元--
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在只要1萬美金 , 下一年就有1千美金
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	拿到百元美金後的那一年 , 送或花一年的時間
that's how fast this is moving .	移動的速度就這麼快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這是小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和水槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在醫院 , 孩子的肚子像饑荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是說 , 當他吃下肚時 , 他的腸道基本上打開了 , 排泄物溢出到他的腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百次手術之後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 , 我現在好多痛苦啊 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒童科醫師恰巧有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因組定序做好 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	牠們發現的是在一個控制細胞死亡的基因上有一處單點變異
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是說 , 他對食物的本質產生了免疫反應 , 那是很自然的反應 , 這導致細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制這些基因的確是壞掉了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這也說明了很多事情 , 當然 , 其中一種治療骨髓移植的方法 , 是他做骨髓移植的 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的努力恢復 , 他現在在吃沾著a1醬汁的牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	把基因組當作普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身上了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 這裡
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	它對我們所有人的意義是 , 在這個房間裡的每個人 , 都可以多活五年、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事情 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你能想到地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們有能力追上糧食生產 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也用在種植新的一道玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 及其他對乾旱、洪水、害蟲和農藥的作物上 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在看來 , 只要我們繼續增加人口我們就必須繼續種植和食用經過基因改造過的食物而這也是我今天唯一要做的
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有沒有人願意自願不再吃東西 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 沒有一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一部打字機 , 數十年來 , 所有桌上型電腦的主要設計 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上被這台機器刪除了 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	接著 , 文字處理器的普遍版本出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但 , 最終 , 它是一個顛覆性的顛覆 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	bobmetcalfe發明了以太網連接所有這些電腦徹底地改變了一切
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們還有雅虎還有整個網路泡沫化 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不過不用擔心 , 很快地就被ipod , facebook和憤怒的小鳥拯救了 。

so what i'd like you to consider is: what does it mean when these dots don't represent the individual bases of your genome , but they connect to genomes all across the planet ?	所以 , 我想請各位思考的是:當這些點並不代表你基因組的個別基礎 , 但它們連結到整個地球的基因組時 , 是甚麼意思 ?
so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我最近剛買了人命保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我被要求回答:a.我從未有過基因測試 , b.我有過 , 你看 , c.我有過基因測試 , 我沒說過 。
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我能回答a , 我誠實地說 , 以防我的生命保險經紀人在聽演講 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我說的是c會發生什麼事 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	基因組學的消費者應用會蓬勃發展 。
do you want to see whether you're genetically compatible with your girlfriend ? sure .	你想知道你是不是跟女朋友基因上是不是相符 ? 當然 。

there's already a lab today that tests for allele 334 of the avpr1 gene , the socalled cheating gene .	今天已經有實驗室在測試avpr1基因的allele334 , 也就是所謂的欺騙基因 。
so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天在場的各位 , 若有其他重要的人 , 轉過身去找他們 , 換成他們的嘴巴 , 送到實驗室 , 然後你就會知道了 。

now think of it , it's 2016 and the leading candidate releases not only her four years of back tax returns , but also her personal genome .	想想看 , 2016年 , 領先的候選人不僅釋放了她過去四年的稅收 , 也釋放了她個人的基因組 。
and it looks really good .	看起來真的很棒 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但 , 想像一下 , 如果我的基因被辨識出來 , 坐在軟體中 , 第三個表親的基因組也坐在那兒 , 且有軟體可以比較這兩者 , 做這些關聯 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫來展示他的骨髓採取器一個新裝置 , 它能很快取得生命的骨髓 , 帶給最少捐贈者 。 他強調在骨髓中找到的成人幹細胞可以用來治療許多臨終的條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一種更好的方法來收集骨髓
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	所以 , 我是史丹佛大學的小兒科癌症醫師及幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床研究重心是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	如今 , 靈感來自jillboltetaylor去年 , 我沒有帶一個人的腦袋 , 但我帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 其實是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 他們大部分都有較先進的惡性 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛移植獎學金 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 還有bob這裡 , 是一位自願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓發送到全國各地 , 拯救有白血病的孩童 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	實際上我們是如何收集這塊骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個完整的o.r.團隊、麻醉醫師、護士 , 以及我對面的另一位醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們將這一小根針 , 你知道 , 不要太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是把這個針筒放在軟組織裡 , 每一次針筒裡穿刺一下硬骨頭、插到tuchus裡 。 用針筒打出大概十毫升骨髓 ,
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	再交給護士 。 她將它注入到一個錫罐 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	再交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次--通常
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到這裡結束時 , 我的手臂酸痛 , 我手上有這麼一個呼叫號 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股尾端看起來就像這個了 , 像個瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以 , 我在想 , 你知道的 , 這項手術在大約40年內並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	應該有更好的做法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以 , 我想到一個微創的方法 , 一個我們稱為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新儀器 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而 「 骨髓採取器 」 , 它的運作方式如下:
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	相對於進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入臀部的前面 , 或後面的後部 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有個很靈活的、有力的導管 , 有一個特別的電線圈 , 它會留在骨髓的顱內 , 順著臀部的輪廓 , 當它四處移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以這使得你能夠快速的期望 , 或吸取骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同一個入口多次 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	因此 , 非常快的 , bob只需一個刺穿 , 局部麻醉 , 將之作為一個門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小額資金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個
and our team members developed this technology .	我們團隊的成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物 , 以及豬研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	出乎我們意料 , 我們不僅僅發現了骨髓 , 還發現了從骨髓採取器採取的幹細胞活性 , 相較於正常的裝置 , 相較於正常的骨髓採取器 , 我們的骨髓細胞活性增加了十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡有個病人 , 你可以在有彈性的曲線附近看到它
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩條路過同一個病人 , 來自同一個洞
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉、門診以後所進行的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	比起標準的方法 , 同一個病人 , 我們得到了大約三到六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 ,
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	它們潛力無窮 , 但還未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人的幹細胞遍及我們的全身 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液幹細胞 , 我們已經用這種幹細胞療法40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年 , 有爆炸性的骨髓幹細胞運用骨髓幹細胞來治療病患的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、骨科用藥、組織工程 , 甚至是神經系統用以治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛公佈 , 正在商業化今年2.0世代 「 骨髓採取器 」
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望可以取出更多幹細胞 , 轉化為更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在年輕時還能銀行買到自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 以便在未來能用到它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi提出了一個有爭議的宇宙新模型這可能可以解答所有重大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西的話 , 這是最美好的 「 八維模型 」 存在於基本粒子和 「 原子力 」 中 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	嘉瑞特.利西對他的萬物理論的解釋
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看這些致命方程式吧 , 真可愛 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 在接下來的十八分鐘裡我會盡力在不用方程式的前提之下描述粒子物理的美好
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗和不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚的頭部都由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地繁殖和分枝 , 成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級聰明的珊瑚我們就能在單獨的珊瑚上問他一個合理的問題
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他究竟是如何走到這個特定的地點 , 與他的鄰居作比較 , 如果是剛好的機會 , 或命運 , 又或者是什麽 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們被告知將溫度調高過高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以說是相當重要的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪式的疤痕證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這一池水會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居也是一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他所有地點 , 但身為獨立的個體 , 體驗到不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說分支長進不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 高智商的珊瑚可以獨一無二地準備了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實世界就像珊瑚一樣 , 一直延伸到不同的可能性中 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 將心思擺在眼前是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的怪現象最初是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這組裝中 , 薛丁格待在一個有放射物質的箱子中 , 根據量子力學定律 , 量子力學定律 , 將部門分成一個沒有放射線的狀態 , 一個沒有的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本放射的分支中 , 它會啟動釋放毒藥的觸發器 , 薛丁格則是死亡 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都能分別感受到這些現實
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	據我所知 , 另一隻並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格在這裡 , 是種不同可能性的珊瑚組成 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來做總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 都可以做
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都發生了 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	剩下的物理就是要描述什麼可能會發生 , 什麼不會發生 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可經由幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要講的是我們對這些粒子的了解它們是什麼以及這個平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一束質子和反質子被加速到接近光速的速度 , 並以相撞的速度結合在一起 , 產生出爆炸的純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這些能量會立刻轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 與探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器-日內瓦的大型強子對撞機周長有17英哩的範圍 , 運行時它所吸引的電力相當於蒙特雷市的5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測哪些粒子會在每一次的碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們什麼是粒子可以產生的 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和質子和反質子所攜帶的能量都一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這限制更重大的粒子都不會產生 , 也不會對我們保持隱形 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器令人相當興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越七倍的能量極限放在前所未有的能量極限所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們可能看見的事物之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子的一整個動物園 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座很多人都過得很好的生活 , 把他們推到一旁
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中和的合作夥伴叫做中子不帶電且有著極小的質量
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下夸克有很大的質量 , 將三者結合 , 使原子內的質子與中子結合 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些粒子分為兩類左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代電量與第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和各種力量產生交互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	帶電粒子通過光子傳遞電磁力相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	有一個非常微弱的力量 , 被稱為 「 極度微弱的力量 」 , 和 「 左撇子 」 互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同載荷 , 稱作色荷 , 並且有三種不同品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以責怪莫瑞•蓋爾曼這些名字──它們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力 , 它的質量和物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷和物質發生作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見但我們很確定存在的粒子就是希格斯粒子它給予所有其他粒子的質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是觀察希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確信它會成真 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們可能還能看到的
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我會在演講結束前向各位展示這美好的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算所有不同的粒子共有226種
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那會有很多粒子可以持續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子是很奇怪的
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 就會出現一些美麗的圖案 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子擁有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克生成的質子合成時 , 它會有總電荷加一加一 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 它們的載荷相反 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	現在 , 電荷實際上是另外兩個載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這種模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	稱為電弱統一模型於1967年組裝完成
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大多數人只熟悉電荷而不是兩者皆同是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力較弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	既然大量的希格斯粒子會沿著圖的水平方向移動 , 那麼電磁力的光子就會維持無質量 , 在載荷空間中和電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力就由兩度空間中的粒子載荷的型式所描述
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後把載荷用夸克形式沿著這些方向繪製出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中畫出來 , 然後投射到二度空間 , 這樣我們就可以看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用自然會在這四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞會產生能量四個載荷方向的載荷總量為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這一刻 , 任何東西只要有著相同的能量 , 就可以產生出總負荷為零的能量 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 以便更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這有著一個很好的對稱六角形 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子的粒子 , 例如這個 , 會和有色夸克相互作用 , 比如這個綠夸克 , 給夸克一個不同的色荷量--這個紅夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每一個原子裏發生上百萬次使原子核保持一體
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但對應三個作用力的這四種載荷並未終結
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再納入兩個載荷相對應到引力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些加進去 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的自旋載荷 , 自旋向下和自旋向下 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中呈現出很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這模式符合我們對於大自然在微小的粒子尺度下如何被建造的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們能確定的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子是實驗所能達到的極限
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道了這些小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙與這些小尺度一起運作的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談關於我們尚未知道的新舊觀念 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否取得整個enchilada 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成宇宙全貌的粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 當實驗到達更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷圖案 , 這種不太對稱 , 可以從更完美的圖案中浮現 , 很類似希格斯粒子如何打破電弱圖案以產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引入新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們要導入一個新的方向時 , 我們能猜出在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷 , 然後我們就能讓它和其他顆粒一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜測明智的話 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中構建標準載荷集 , 作為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的對稱組成對稱 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個選擇與1973年由帕提和薩拉姆推出的一個大統一理論相呼應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的合成圖案 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 粒子似乎在缺少的地方 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 把已知的模式納入為 「 子集 」 的結構 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案讓我們得以預測那些從未見過的粒子的存在
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該和弱力很相似 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質擁有和第一代物質擁有完全相同的載荷
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子通過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間上彼此相連
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以賦予每一個粒子獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代用一種叫 " 三重性 " 的對稱性和第一代相關聯
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最漂亮的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一點都對應到這個複雜而漂亮的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的彎曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何構造可以描述宇宙怎麼用最小的尺度運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	在這八度載荷空間中這個形狀的形狀是非常美麗的 , 它可以概括成千上萬種這些基本粒子間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的表面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到包含其中的許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過特定的旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿著對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是非常美麗的物體 , 如同其他統一理論一樣 , 我們可以看到一些孔洞在這些圖案中 , 新粒子是被這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	在這有20個空格需要新粒子其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置上 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該像希格斯粒子一樣稀少的原子 , 但具有顏色的載荷和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著很深的數學字根
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	許多人認為它是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個了不起的前景一個偉大數學美麗的物體可以用可想像的最小尺度描述粒子相互作用的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的這個想法一點也不新穎 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫下這句話: 「 大自然的大本書 , 一直站在我們的眼前 , 都用數學的語言寫出來 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他的幾何形狀 , 沒有了這些 , 根本不可能理解它的任何字 ; 沒有了這些 , 就會有一個在黑暗的迷宮中遊走 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學性
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以像是一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但可以確保數學的核心是純粹而美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學一起形成的數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用著一個美麗的圖案
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著圖案的使用像是大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器時 , 我們也許能夠知道大自然是否使用這種e8圖案或另一種模式 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一段很棒的探險旅程
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就非常非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然也不利於我個人
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還不錯 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作是個很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論及其它類似的理論都是長時間的結果 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部分這些想法可能最後都不會對自然界成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有大量的毀滅 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	這樣看來 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司所做的一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同對任何大型投資來的 , 在沒有成功的情況下 , 要放棄一系列的研究 , 在情感上是很難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西沒有用 , 你就得要丟掉它 , 再試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在這種不確定中 , 唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和透視 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已竭盡所能地過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡我三個載荷的方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我所從事的物理學也沒有實現 , 我仍然知道我曾經過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	並試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是我父母最大的謎團之一 , 就是我怎樣在這樣的環境下活下去而不去像全職工作一樣全職工作 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家鄉辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象類似 , 但在稍微不同的位置 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難 , 但卻能讓我住在美麗的地方 , 且在我人生中能保持平衡 , 讓我很高興 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚混在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也非常享受超級聰明人的陪伴 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請到ted來 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能明白其中的2% , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以接下來我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我習慣了珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 能讓少數人興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它能把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你的意思是我們應該想出宇宙的核心 , 那些最微小的事物 , 似乎就是e8物體的可能性嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我是說 , 有沒有一個量表可以達到最小的程度 ? 或...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在 , 我給你們看的模式 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理原理相對應到一個很漂亮的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的那個我們知道是肯定的
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似性 , 與其符合e8圖案的形狀 , 可能是其他的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 其實代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它們在我們經歷的空間中 , 會被扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有我們看到的基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 就我所理解的 , 用更小的弦震動方式來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在內部震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子與e8的關聯呢 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不 , 它會是e8型狀對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時它會扭曲的方向 , 就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 安:e8形狀的大小 , 電子的大小 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	對於我的照片 , 我感覺到是需要的 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	大一點嗎 ? 小一點嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:就我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都同時在擴展和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是我為什麼用這比喻來做珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的進入方式將會是一個連接時空中每一點的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲方向就是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們會把自己當成點來表現 , 用這種方式來互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能講得更清楚
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了一種奇蹟 , 我當然想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常感謝大家的到來 。 這真是太棒了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳說中的黑猩猩研究員珍古德說到塔卡爾還有其它的社區計畫 , 這些計畫幫助非洲城鎮的居民肩並肩生活充滿威脅的動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德能幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以這樣說 , 斷氣囊 , 良好氣味可以這樣但我們也可以ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所接的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一處 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想談談的主題 , 從昨天的模式裡拿起 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論的是一個神奇的三歲澳洲小孩selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過透過基因圖譜 , 關於人類歷史、族譜、關於人類的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一名古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯利基 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩之路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時是相當非比尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	目前是很普遍的做法 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石得知它們看起來是什麼樣子從肌肉連接的形狀來判斷它們是如何從各式各樣與它們相關的文物來判斷這些行為
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然行為並不是化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他提出一個現在普遍的理論 , 如果我們發現行為模式相似或相同的現象發生在我們現存最接近的物種--人猿 , 以及今天的人類 , 也許這些行為是在七百萬年前出現在人猿類型的 , 像人類的祖先中 ,
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們將這些特質從古老的歷史中帶著走過來
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你去看現今處理人類進化的教科書 , 你經常會發現人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比任何其他生物更像我們 , 在這個ted會議中我們也聽過這種現象 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 黑猩猩在某些方面和我們很像 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 , 牠們可以活到六十歲或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部份的牠們應該不會在野外活到六十歲了 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	溫柔先生 , 母羊在十一到十二歲時生了她的第一個小孩 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她的小孩每五、六年就只有一個 , 是童年長期依賴期間 , 當孩子在哺育時 , 晚上和母親一起睡 , 和她的背一起騎 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的孩童期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們也一樣 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化過程中變得越來越複雜 , 所以我們發現在個體的生命歷史中 , 學習扮演著越來越重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 透過這種方式 , 現已在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中看到不同的使用工具的方式 , 這些行為如何從一個世代的傳承到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 才能形容這些使用工具的行為為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口說的語言 , 我們已經談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確擁有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多都相似 , 甚至一模一樣的姿勢 , 在同樣的情境中形成 。 迎接黑猩猩的擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們還會親吻、握手、拍打牠的背部 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們會大搖大搖大搖大擺地投擲石塊 ,
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們會發現很多的例子都是有同情心的、有愛的、真正利他行為的前兆 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 就像我們人類一樣 , 牠們也有天生的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們有著極端殘暴的能力 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分來說 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體來進行 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們是十分具侵略性的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們瞭解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物世界之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條界線非常的模糊 , 並且在我們做出更多的觀察時 , 它變得越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍在持續進行 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會關係中的黑猩猩們 , 比起其他任何事情 , 都更為幫助我們意識到自己也是其中的一份子 , 而不是與眾不同 , 那些與我們共享地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很遺憾地發現 , 黑猩猩們就像世界上許多生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 上面顯示了岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	我在16年前飛越整個區域時 , 才意識到 , 在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時 , 它沿著坦岡易科湖東面的沿岸幾乎沒有破壞 , 它就是那個小小的 , 30平方英呎的岡貝國家公園所在之處 , 有一個問題出現在我腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們該如何拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 , 當住在國家公園附近的人們正為了生存而苦苦掙扎時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	住在那裡的人 , 比這片土地可能支持的還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	持續增加的難民們如洪水般從蒲隆地湧入並從剛果湖邊游過來
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人們 , 他們買不起他們在其他地方買來的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱它為坦尚尼亞造林計劃 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常整體的方式 , 改善住在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	一開始是小規模的 , 有12個村莊 。 現在是24個村莊了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間詳細說明 , 但它包含了諸如樹木的哺乳類 , 養殖最適合這種已退化、幾乎像沙漠的土地 , 沿著這些山脈上的土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤流失的方法
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 這樣在兩年內可以再次生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力幫助村民們從井裡獲取淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們機會給小額貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	而世界各地的案例中 , 大約有95%的貸款都退還了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權女性 , 與教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 這樣她們才能完成中等學業 。 清楚地知道 , 隨著女性的教育 , 全世界的尺寸都提升了 , 家庭人數減少 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供節育計畫和愛滋病相關的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育計畫有所改變 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育工作的成果是讓住在這24個村莊的農夫們 , 不要把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順便一提 , 很多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 是一支坦尚尼亞人的隊伍 , 要去那些村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦桑尼亞的團隊與村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 隨著山丘的上層佈滿了樹木 , 所以你得到了這片可怕的土壤侵蝕和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在開發更大的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠超出國家公園 , 延伸到所有這些非常貧瘠的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實也同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地保留下來 , 所以再一次的 , 當樹木長回來之後 , 黑猩猩們就會長出葉門廊道 , 藉此可以和國家公園外的其它遺跡族群互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 坦尚尼亞造林是個成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製到非洲的其它區域 , 其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野區域 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們前面這幾天一直在討論的 , 都是很重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有著很大的貧窮
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有許多人居住在土地上 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 土壤開放給腐化的土壤 , 當絕望的人口砍伐愈來愈多的樹木 , 他們就能嘗試種植食物給自己和家人 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要付出代價 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他問題不只在非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家的問題 , 的確 , 無所不在地 , 我們對自己的星球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人都能維持像歐洲人或美國人一樣的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的地球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說四種 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	究竟發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這個問題在這兒 , 我們是可以說是地球上行走最有智慧的生物 , 擁有非凡的頭腦 , 能夠用這麼好看的科技 , 來說明這些ted研討會所造成的影響 , 然而我們卻是在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民在做出重大決策之前 , 曾坐下來問他們自己: 「 這項決策如何影響我們前進的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我在這裡談的不是非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是以: 「 這會如何影響下次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行時 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 他們消失的森林 , 我了解到更多的是 , 非洲許多的問題可能就在上次殖民時期被剝削過後 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 前往亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	不論在哪裡 , 都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而你知道我在說的那個 。 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 ,
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是我們本世紀所要面對的最關鍵的課題之一 , 到處都是水受到農業、工業和家庭化學品污染 , 這些化學物仍然被世界各地噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯造成的效應更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤流失 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不計後果的燃燒化石燃料加上其他溫室氣體 , 所以說 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候出現了一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候混雜在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且更受影響的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經受影響的非洲 ,
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱狀況更加嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 水災又會增加 , 貧窮、飢餓與疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在無法支撐的土地面積 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 無法搬離的人數 , 因為整個土地都退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以沙漠化愈來愈多 , 愈來愈嚴重 , 隨著上一棵樹遭到砍伐 , 愈來愈詭異 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只發生在非洲 , 全世界
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可以有某種程度的斷續續續性嗎 ? 這種非常聰明的大腦 , 可以是ted科技能展現出來的 , 而人類心智 ? 用非科學的角度來看待它 , 以愛和同情心來說 。 有沒有一些斷續的 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 或冷漠的 , 或痛苦和憤怒的 。 他們說的或多或少都是一樣的 。 「 我們會這樣想 , 因為我們覺得你已經損害了我們的未來 , 卻束手無策 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經降低了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 就會想 , 從我還是他們年紀開始 , 我們是如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我感受到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這個計畫就是我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 這個計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經散播到世界各地97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它有象徵意義 。 根形成堅固的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來很小 ; 為了要到達陽光 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上所造成的所有問題 , 環保和社會問題 。 這是關於希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以突破這困擾 , 可以為所有生物創造出更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	" 根與芽 " 計畫所傳達最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每天都能做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇權 。 每一個在這間會議室的人 , 我們都可以選擇要做什麼樣的差別 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇這取決於我們要改變事情讓窮人也能選擇
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體都會選出三個計劃 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 以及哪個國家 , 不論是在城市或鄉村 , 都一樣是哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼稚園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始做他們自己的根與芽計畫 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每一個小組都會在它們之間做選擇 , 三個不同類型的專案計畫 , 讓這個世界更美好 , 認知到這些不同的問題互相連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們其中一個計畫 , 是要協助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	再來 , 如果他們能做到 , 他們可能會募集資金來幫助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物們 , 不只是野生的動物們 , 還有家養的動物們 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫將是幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一路上 , 編織出一個訊息 , 就是學習去以和平與和諧的方式生活在我們自己、我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、國家、文化、文化 , 和我們與自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能再以我們既有的速度摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們擁有的不只是這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選其中一個或兩個在非洲的計畫 , 根與芽的團體正在進行 , 一或兩項計畫只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果 , 獅子山共和國、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其它的團體 。 正如我所說 , 目前在全球97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹木 。 他們在種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 和雞在一起 , 以一點點的錢賣蛋 , 或只是用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 感受到一種驕傲和自主權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依靠別人的蔬菜與雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	在烏干達也正在使用它 , 提供一些心理協助給兒童軍人 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣子的計畫 , 就是將他們自生自滅 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間更多的根與芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的非常重要的成份 , 比較年長的孩子和比較年輕的孩子說話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而非自願性的懷孕之類的年輕人會傾聽其他的年輕人而非成年人
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過那麼多糟糕的事情 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬隻的數量 , 在本世紀之初 , 沒有超過十五萬隻的數量 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的地方沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣沒有希望的會議 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是神奇的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想技術
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我實在太激動了 , 到了人們談論堆肥式廁所的時候 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往廁所邊沖 , 情況很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否曾為我們的孩子關心這個星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否關心他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎它們的未來 , 我們身為世界上精英的精英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出一些選擇 , 作為我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 我們穿什麼
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他長大後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或不論是什麼 ,
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人類的大腦 , 與人的心結合 , 我們就牽手到世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted能幫助我們的原因 , google也幫我們 , esri也幫我們繪製岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在 , 來連結它們 , 它開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽過了 , 現在開始
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這個改變 , 這個改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 我們必須看到這些改變 。
