and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個對希望的理由是令人驚異的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一塊完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要有時間 , 或許再一些能協助它再生的區域 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而坦尚尼亞造林計劃就是個例子 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我說過 , 看似已死去的樹木就不會再被砍伐了 , 因為你已經有了很多的木材 , 然後在五年之內 , 你就可以有一棵30英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎瀕臨絕種的生物 , 可以有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這鼓舞了我 。 這讓我想到我最後一個希望類別 。 在過去的兩天中 , 我們聽到了這麼多的事 。 這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人們堅決的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 或其他那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 將他們自己從中抽離出來 , 有時只要有助於他們 , 將自己的那一舉在社會中 , 並且讓他們成為改變這個世界的一份子 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	試想一下 , 從非洲來的一到兩位 , 都是非常鼓舞人心的 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一個很長的清單 , 但顯然尼爾森•曼德拉從17年的辛勤勞工中湧現出來 , 23年的監禁 , 有很了不起的寬恕 , 這樣他就能領導他的國家在沒有血腥對抗的情況下 , 達成了種族隔離的邪惡政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的kensarowiwa對著這家大型的石油公司進行雖然世界各地的人們竭盡所能地被處決
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是多麼的鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 就是我們所需要的年輕非洲人的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境榜樣 , 今天也聽過一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會再次與在ted的各位分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	在那個會議上 , 管理整個會議中心的年輕女子最後發了最後一個詞 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書 , 十分興奮 。 她是根與芽的槍 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她當時在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這能幫助她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常非常興奮 , 能與她見面 , 僅僅是一個例子 , 關於年輕人當他們有權力時 , 給予他們機會去行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 在海洋中、在我們的生活中 , 以及思考著如何將我們自己從塑膠漩渦中解放出來 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色使命──藍色、海洋、塑膠、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我與塑膠袋一起工作 , 我切開 , 縫合起來 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 在過去二十年間 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩個和三度空間的碎片 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我和塑膠一起工作 , 我的一些作品開始產生裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 ,
it's ephemeral just like us . "	簡直就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在更進一步的教育我自己 , 更進一步去了解塑膠 , 事實上我意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是一件壞事 , 塑膠會分解成小碎片 , 因為它永遠都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	而我們發現在海洋環境裡 , 很多的
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我一開始的反應--我想這是很多人第一次意識到這件事情 " 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以事實上我和一艘貨船出海的提案和兩艘退休的拖網漁船、起重機、一台拖網機、一台拖網機 , 和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是要出去垃圾漩渦 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始把塑膠磨碎 , 放進一點點冰冷的模塊裡 , 做成可能被用來建設在未開發的社區裡的建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過垃圾漩渦去研究塑膠問題的人聊聊 , 他們研究海洋環境的塑膠問題 。 這樣做之後 , 我發現 , 要清理塑膠的塑膠 , 相對於全世界每天實際上產生的量 , 我必須退一步 , 看看更大的狀況 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	大局就是:我們得想個辦法把水龍頭關掉 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單次使用和丟棄的塑膠碎片 , 這些都是每天進入海洋環境的 , 且是以全球性的規模在進行 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以從這點來看 , 我也發現我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心你在想在太平洋的中間的塑膠 , 我發現現在有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦 , 可能是全球五大洋中五大洋的塑膠垃圾 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦還有超市裡的塑膠垃圾漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超級市場 , 我所有的食物都是塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都以塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康食品市場都包裝 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠滲出到我們體內的毒素
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群在研究這個問題的人聚在一起 , 我們成立了 「 塑膠污染聯盟 」 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫在進行 , 但有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其中之一是:如果我們在海洋裡發現的80%到90%是我們在海洋裡發現的垃圾是塑膠的 , 那麼我們為什麼不叫它做原料呢 ?
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	資源回收 , 所有人都將書的內容以永續和綠色環保再利用資源回收的概念終結
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	把一些東西放到垃圾桶裡 , 然後就不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	實情是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比例不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入探究 , 尤其是談到塑膠瓶 , 大部分只能降級回收、焚化、送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降級回收 , 變成較少的物品 , 玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或是再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再次變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是一個大問題
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一個我們觀察並要求人們去思考的問題是我們已在 " 減量、再利用、回收 " 前面加上第四個r " 這樣就拒絕了
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	儘管可能的話 , 拒絕使用單一及用過即丟的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有一些是非常老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在在收集這些超酷的pyrex貨櫃 , 用它們來取代玻璃、保鮮盒 , 來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一個不銹鋼瓶子或是玻璃瓶都很容易 , 如果你去旅行 , 你已經忘記帶一個不鏽鋼瓶裝水 , 或過濾水 , 相對之下 , 購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在場的各位說些什麼──我知道你們對這個議題了解很多──就是這在海洋裡是個很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者所創造出的問題 , 可以解決的一個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由喚起大家的意識來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇一些替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 當可能性地選擇單使用塑膠的替代品時 ,
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這條線路切割成我們的海洋 , 藉此 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這段來自麻省理工學院的帕蒂梅斯實驗室的示範影片 , 由普納夫婦所領導 , 是ted的雜誌 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 有一個投影機 , 為和我們的環境創造了深刻的互動 。 想像 「 關鍵報告 」 , 然後 , 一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範、設計、界面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂摩斯和帕納•密特里•德萊克梅斯的第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 關於我們能否進化出或發展出第六感 , 一種能讓我們幾乎接觸到新陳代謝或存在某處可能有重要性的資訊 , 能協助我們做出對的決策 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們有些人可能會認為 , 現今的手機不就已經做到這點嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與別人會面時--當然這就是最好的社交場所--一年中 , 你不跟某人握手然後說 , " 你能等一下嗎我拿出手機用google查詢你 ? "
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你到超級市場站在那巨大的廁所衛生紙走道時 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 上一個網站 , 去決定這些不同的衛生紙中哪種購買是最環保的 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們無法很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 能協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 且不需要使用者改變他們的任何行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我在這裡揭露我們最近的努力 , 也是最成功的努力 , 到目前為止 , 這仍然是個很有成效的過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我身上正戴著這個裝置 , 我們把零件從架子上拆下來 , 再把零件組裝起來 , 順便一提 , 到目前為止 , 只需花350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我帶著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式、用電池驅動的投影系統 , 只有一點點鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些組件向我口袋裡的手機通訊 , 它就像是通訊和計算的裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生 , 普納•米特里 , 他真的是天才 , 一直在執行和設計這整個系統 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何平面前 , 開始用他的手去與投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻顯著手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著大家可能認得的簡單標記帽子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他做過的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他可以直接去一幅長灘的地圖拉近和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 例如 「 照相 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的事物 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	然後當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆前 , 將他拍的所有照片投影出來 , 整理這些照片 , 然後再用所有自然的手勢把它們重新排列起來 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前你們其中一些人可能也在現場看過jeffhan的示範或許有人會想: 「 這不是很像微軟的平面嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這兩者的差別在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何平面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以取得 , 和這個投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜式的 , 也可以是──
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 一個重要的不同點是 , 它完全是移動式的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點是量產後它的成本不會比現在的手機明天還高而且不會變成一個更大的包裝看起來比我脖子上掛的這個版本還要時髦的多
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們其中一些人覺得自己像是tomcruise在 " 關鍵報告 " 裡一樣酷的感覺 , 我們對於這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因是它真的可以扮演這六感裝置中的其中之一 , 它可以給你有關你面前事物的重要資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超級市場去買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品 , 系統可以辨識出他所拿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 在他的個人標準下 , 這個選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想拿出最多漂白劑的衛生紙來吃 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以取得亞馬遜書局的評分 。 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順便一提 , 在亞馬遜網站得到了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納轉了這本書的頁面 , 然後可以看到額外的資訊 , 關於這本書的讀者評論 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家所提供的資訊 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到某個特定的頁面 , 他會找到我們一位朋友的專家 , 給他額外的資訊 , 關於特定頁面的任何資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時--它從來不需要過時--
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到關於你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解 , 可以得到最新的運動分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與別人互動時 , 也許你可以看到一個字雲 , 上面的標籤 , 和那個人相關的字句在他們的部落格及個人網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的飛機被延遲了 , 登機門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在是什麼時間 , 那就跟在手臂上手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以這就是我們目前正在開發的第六感讓我們可以無縫接觸所有相關的資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 跟我說的一樣 , 背後的天才 ,
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很大的掌聲 , 因為我覺得他在過去的三個月中並沒有睡多少 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他不太高興 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不夠完美 , 還差得遠 。 還在持續進行當中 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 或許再十年後我們會帶著植入腦內的終極第六感來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲斯.羅德里格斯和艾爾瓦菲都因無法想像的損失而生 , 羅德里奎茲的兒子在世界貿易中心於2001年9月11日被殺 ; 埃瓦菲的兒子zacariasmoussaui因襲擊而被判有罪 , 並且被判終身監禁 。 希望找到和平 , 這兩位母親也得以進一步了解另一位 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911療癒:那些發現寬恕、友誼的母親們 ,
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉思•羅德里奎茲:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說卻是很自然的 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次得知我兒子是在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在直到36小時後死去 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼 , 以我們兒子之名──我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時──然而 , 透過驚嚇 , 震驚 , 和我們生命中可怕的爆炸──真的 , 我們沒有要報仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後當zacariasmoussaui被指控六項對恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑如果罪名成立的話 , 我和我的丈夫對此反對 , 公開反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那也透過人權組織 , 我們和其他受害者家屬一起被聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時也過來了 , 我心想: 「 真是一個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	總有一天 , 我會想見那位女士 , 當我強壯一點的時候 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍在深深的哀傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有這份力氣 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道總有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當別人聽到我兒子是受害者 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子所被指控的事 , 她並沒有得到這樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦就等於我了 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年十一月見面 , 現在aicha會告訴你這一切是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	艾克•艾瓦菲:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我也要求人權組織讓我和受害者的父母親聯絡 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是整個團體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟、姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼睛裡看到 , 她也是一個母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為一個母親 , 我遭受很大的痛苦
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 那是我十六歲時失去的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以對zacarias的故事實在是太過分了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然痛苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他還活著 。 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這麼一來 , 我的痛苦才是其他女性的正面影響 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性這是為我們 , 為我們女性為我們的孩子
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我講反抗暴力 , 反抗恐怖主義 ,
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我到學校去和年輕的 , 穆斯林女孩談 , 讓他們不接受針對她們的意志 , 非常年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們跟我一樣的結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我站在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到很多東西從那天開始我們第一次見到其他的家人-這是一個私人的和安全的會面 , 因為那時是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個時候的超級愛國主義---我們這些家庭成員們 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想跟我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她就緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想見她呢 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們就已經欣然大哭了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們圍成一個圈 , 有支援 , 有協助 , 從人們體驗到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	由aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無罪 , 但我想告訴你 , 我是如何為你的家人所發生的事感到難過 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎樣的苦痛 , 我覺得如果犯罪 , 人應該被公平審判 , 受到懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她就是用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我很想說 , 那是個破冰者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	那時發生的事 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 身為人類 , 我們都連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午快結束的時候---大概是午餐後的三小時---我們彷彿彼此認識了一輩子 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 不僅是女人 , 在現今的情況下 , 能夠如此慷慨 , 以及當時在她兒子做了什麼 , 和她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼辛苦的人 , 從這樣完全不同的文化和環境和我的環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的聯繫我非常重視
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都和害怕他人有關 , 但踏出這一步接著發現: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能和誰見面 , 不知道我是誰 , 或是我和誰有這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們必須試著去認識其他人 , 去認識其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也必須要寬容 , 你的心念必須要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要能忍受
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天 , 我們都能以和平共處 , 彼此尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多無法取得乾淨的飲用水了 。 工程師麥可普立查做了點事情 , 發明了可攜式的生命體過濾器 , 它可以在幾秒鐘內讓最多人喝水 。 這是來自tedglobal2009的驚人示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	麥可pritchard的水過濾器轉變成髒水可以飲用 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	我今天想談兩件事情
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都享受著這會議所提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 ,
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得它來自於安全源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自於像這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數字會說 , 你們之中有一半的人現在都得了痢疾 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過許多關於統計和提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎是無法通過
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 用當前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 以致於無法思索地解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們直接關掉:我們、政府、和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓大家知道透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全世界有13 , 000人正在腹瀉患者 。
and four children have just died .	而且四個小孩剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶是因為我生氣了
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大多數人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節的隔天 , 看著亞洲海嘯摧毀性的新聞 , 在電視上大放上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾天和幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的令我無法置信 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風襲擊美國邊緣 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道這花了五天才把水運到超級巨怪嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街道上互相射殺電視節目和水
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時 , 我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 還有在我的廚房裡 , 讓我妻子很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型後 , 我終於做出這個 , lifesaver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談一下科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌 , 大約200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	那肯定會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救命員的氣孔只有15奈米大小 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有任何東西能順利通過
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下

but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 要知道 , 如果我們身在發生水災的災區孟加拉 , 水不會像這樣 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的作用很簡單

today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個水壺來展示給大家看 。 讓我們拿一點那把大便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠髒 , 我們來稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 那我要把這非常骯髒的水 , 放進這裏來 。 你還想要喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 。 可以了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些打氣筒 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	那些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	現在只要我跳過這個茶 , 無菌的飲用水就會跑出來
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我必須要快點 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	完成了 。 小心電器 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	什麼是它的味道 ?

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 世界各地成千上萬的人使用了lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	會維持6000公升
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 利用故障安全技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把馬桶拿出來 , 把一個新的進去 ,
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	又高又6000公升的電力
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看它的應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾個禮拜後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個營地會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 。 更多的資源被需要
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會自行延續下去
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考方式 , 再把這些運送物資 , 人們就可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 並開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 並不需要天然災害才可行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的思維、國家基礎建設 , 和管道的工作 , 實在是太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你用計算機算數字時 , 事態就用不完了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 不同的思維 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做 , 不如利用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費除去水中鹽分 , 運送到那裡 , 將水倒到山上、河流和溪流中 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。

well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶
or we could use one of these .	或者利用這些
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry罐頭上 ,
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將能處理二萬五千公升的水 ; 對四歲的家庭而言 , 這已經足夠用三年了 。
and how much does it cost ?	到底要花多少錢呢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天大約半分錢可以跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 在用水的時點 , 母親和孩子不再需要一天走四小時來取得他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只需八十億美元 , 我們就可以達成千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	用在環境方面 , 英國政府每年花約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果就是每年有三十五億人受苦 , 每年死亡的兩百萬個兒童都會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•奧許諾聲稱我們正生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力是以從未有的方式在改變的 。 在tedx-brussels的一個咒語中 , 他提出了他所看到的三個重大的全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化文化 ,
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力轉移
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一位非常有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代 , 邱吉爾的腦部迴盪
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這樣寫的: 「 夏日的idle山 , 躺著的溪流 , 哈克 , 我聽到的是遠方的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲音 , 遠的、近的、低沉的 , 路上傳來的聲音 , 親愛的朋友和食物 , 向粉末 , 士兵遊走 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩詞有興趣的人 , 這首詩是《舒洛普郡少女》 , 由豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所理解的 , 也在尼爾森交響樂團中聽過 , 是十九世紀漫長 , 炎熱 , 遍地林木的夏天穩定不穩定 , 即將告一段落 , 我們即將走進歷史的恐怖時期 , 當時權力有所改變 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位女士、先生們 , 總是伴隨著騷動而來的時期 , 也常常是血 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我想要傳達的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 當權力建立的高低點已經開始改變了 , 新的世界觀 , 新的世界存在的權力開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	而這些--我們今天很清楚的看到--幾乎總是非常動盪的時代 , 高難度的時代 , 而且經常是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一句 , 這發生在每個世紀一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生的事情 , 那是休斯曼的感受 , 也和邱吉爾的感受一樣 , 當權力從老國 , 歐洲的舊權力穿越大西洋 , 來到美國的新興強權 , 也就是美國本世紀初的時候 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被投射在兩場血腥的災難上這場災難在第一世紀 , 第二部份:兩場世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲的內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位 , 各位先生女士 , 我們正處於這樣的時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想要談談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	在這之中 , 前兩項 , 大約是權力的轉移
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個 , 是關於我想要提及的一個新的維度 , 它從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們來談談發生在世界的權力轉移 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事 , 在某種意義上 , 很恐怖 , 因為這從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到希臘權力的橫向移轉到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明時期出現的權力移轉 , 但我們看到的有些不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移轉 ,
it's also moving vertically .	也會垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的狀況是 , 受到責任的權力被牽制到法律的規則當中 , 在國家國家的制度下 , 已經開始大量地移居到全球的舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力雖然我們說是全球化市場但事實上卻是全球化權力
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級裡權力是被責任歸屬於法律的層級在國際舞台上則不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台也是現在存在權力的全球舞台:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢改變者的力量──這個巨大貨幣的力量──現在正在循環這筆錢的大貨幣價值32倍 , 是它應有的金錢用品──在金融變革上 , 若你願意 , 最近 , 金融推動我們所有人向大型企業發展的力量──大型預算──現在 , 發展了大筆的預算 , 成了大筆的預算 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球化的空間大致上是沒有受到規範的 , 沒有受到法律的規則所規範的 , 在這個空間中 , 人們行為可能沒有受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	那適合現在的強權對象 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些有權力的人在沒有限制的空間中營運 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 未受法律規範牽制 , 不僅僅是你想要的國際貿易 , 網路 , 等等 。 也因為你不想要的國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的揭示是即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住在那個空間裡的人 , 仍然可以攻擊你──就算在九月一日的一個城市中 , 也是最具代表性的 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	有人說這四百萬美元中的百分之六十拿去資助911恐怖攻擊的經費其實是貫穿雙子星大樓的機構911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播公司 , 讓他們能夠繞過他們的毒藥 , 這關乎破壞我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	早晚 , 早晚晚 , 權力統治者必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年會是一場騷動 , 或多或少有些程度 , 我們就能達成那個目標:將統治者帶上國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我指的不是設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便一提 , 我的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 這是不大可能的做法是擴展更多聯合國的機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 就必須發明
the world needs an international forum .	這世界需要的是一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個手段 , 讓你能將國際行動合理化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但談到全球空間的管理 , 我猜這不會發生 , 透過建立更多聯合國的機構來實現 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 這會發生在有權人聯手 , 做出以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基的協議 , 來管理那個全球性的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你仔細看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為基礎 , 而且強大到連最有權力的國家 , 美國都能在必要的情況下存取 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:努力想創立一個合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道得組一個能夠把統治權帶到那個金融空間的機構為了一個金融的猜想
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團 , 一個合約為底的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題了 , 我們等一下就會回到這裡 , 那就是 , 如果你把最有權力的人聚集在一起 , 來訂定以條約為基礎的制度規則 , 來填補統治空間 , 那麼 , 那些被排除的弱者會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題我們馬上就會回到這問題上
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你要傳遞這些亂流的次數或者多或少 , 那麼我們成功的做法 , 將取決於我們將合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	並且看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和觀眾談談這類的話題 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還會橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說 , 文明的歷史 , 都是第一批出現在大西洋的文明社會 , 最早發生在地中海 , 近期 , 西方後輩在大西洋形成的文明社會 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在正目睹了權力的根本轉變 , 廣義來說 , 遠離那些聚集在大西洋岸邊的國家 , 遠離那些聚集在太平洋邊緣的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	那從經濟實力開始 , 但那是一開始的做法 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增在世界上其他正在成長的強權國家中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這其實不算是從西方轉移到東方 , 有什麼不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於它的價值 , 美國在未來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是世界上最強的國家 , 但她權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 這樣的狀況已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正要走出五十年 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 在這個歷史上 , 我們經歷過一個完全單一化的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一種同情心的需求 , 都必須以它的立場來參考華盛頓這個世界 , 由一個巨型巨型巨型巨型巨人所推崇 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但歷史上卻不常有這種情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在興起的 , 是更正常的歷史事件 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你們已經開始看到多極化的世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家但是在越來越多的強國之中他們會是世界上最強大的國家
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	當然 , 你開始看到中國其他權力建立的中心 , 但我自己的猜測是 , 中國要強大 , 並不是光滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	在自由經濟後 , 中國會開始將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度、巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你愈來愈能看出 , 事實上 , 對我們歐洲人而言 , 世界其實看上去更像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一位偉大的英國外交大臣 , 坎寧閣下 , 曾經形容它是 「 歐洲人的權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡點 , 一個五邊的平衡點
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是以平衡的姿勢在演奏 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供一種平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個被獨立世界統治的時代 , 你有固定的同盟國北約組織 , 華約組織 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	權力的對立意謂著固定的結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力多端的兩極化 , 就表示會轉移和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會越來越常看見我們的同盟國並不是固定不變的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會越來越常見到 , 即使我們西方國家 , 也得要向外伸出 , 穿越大西洋中舒適的圈子 , 要和其他人結盟 , 如果我們想要在世界做到這些事的話 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 光是西方國家是不夠的 , 我們就得帶著其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們得把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我猜伊拉克和阿富汗是最後一次在西方自己試著這麼做 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經達到了400年後的開端 , 我說400年後的奧圖曼帝國的結束 , 因為那是西方強權 , 西方強權 , 西方強權 , 西方強權 , 和西方價值觀的共產 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能一同行動 , 它就能提出、散播到世界各個角落 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是真的 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最近二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 ,
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織布雷頓森林機構--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話進去
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造二十國集團
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我來做個預測 , 預測可能會更嚇人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們已經步入400年後 , 西方國家的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	有人對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與調停 , 世界上的多邊調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 , 爲什麽不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊駐守在藍色貝雷特下 , 揮舞著藍色旗幟 , 揮舞著聯合國的指令 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一人 ?
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	海軍對付索馬利亞海盜的最大內容是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是慈善主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要維持航道暢通
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們沒有共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但和誰合作 , 在那一刻 , 我們會共享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看世界 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	這是第三個因素 , 完全不一樣 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們現代社會 , 因為有網際網路 , 因為人們在這裡談論過的各種事物 , 所有事物都連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是以國家、個人的身分 , 以一種前所未有的方式互相連結 , 前所未有 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關係 , 嗯 , 那一直都存在著
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在 , 我們緊密地被鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你會得到墨西哥的豬流感 , 這是查爾斯戴高樂機場24小時後所面臨的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉 , 大量崩潰
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯大草原發生火災 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深深地互連著 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨自行動的思想 , 沒有與他人建立連結 , 沒有與他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動本身既不受限 , 也不受限於國家本身 , 也不受限於國家本身 , 控制自己的領土 , 因為各國以外的影響現在開始影響到國家內部的發展 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	當時我還是個年輕的大兵 , 在大英帝國戰爭時期
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國防部只關乎一件事 , 只強調一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟國有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當時敵人就在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人則在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在如果我想談談我國防部我得和衛生署談談因為傳染疾病對我的安全造成威脅我得和農業部長談談因為糧食安全對我的國家造成威脅我得和工業部談談因為高科技基礎設施的脆弱性現在是我們的敵人對待我們的敵人就像我們從網路戰爭中看到的一樣我得和內政部談談談因為那些發生在我國家的人身上的糧食安全已經發生在我們國家 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我們的家鄉 , 發生在我們的家鄉 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只和軍人和國防有關 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是把整個機構關起來的能力
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴各位一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直構建的經濟模式 , 建構在工業革命時代的經濟模式上 , 垂直等級制度 , 特殊化的任務 , 指揮結構完全錯了結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位女士、先生們 , 你們在商業上都知道 , 我們這個時代的典範結構就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網路的連結能力很重要 , 不論是政府內部還是外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	下面是第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 不要問我第一條規則和第二條法則 , 因為我還沒發明那些 ; 第三條法則總是比較好聽 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	下面的第三個法則是:在現代 , 所有事情都有關連的時代 , 對於你能做的事 , 最重要的是你能和他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的是你是政府 , 不管你是軍隊 , 不管你是企業你的關鍵 , 是你的財政支援 , 你的內部連接 , 你與他人建立關係的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業上 , 你明白這一點 ; 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但現在最後一件事 ,
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們 , 我們現在以一種前所未有的方式團結在一起 , 那也是我們彼此有相同的命運 ,
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次有了集體的防禦 , 那些一直以來主宰我們國家安全的概念 , 已經不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的強 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的強 , 我就安全了 , 我的盟國 , 像北約組織 , 比他們的同盟國更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	已經不再是
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結以及大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著我與敵人有著越來越多的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是一個外交官在日內瓦和蘇聯協商時 , 在七○年代 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們有著相同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著相同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東地區和平最大的阻礙之一就是以色列人和巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們擁有集體的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位女士、先生們 , 過去有遠見的人和詩人的提案成了我們在公共政策上必須嚴肅地看待這件事 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我以一首詩作為開頭 , 以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	johndonne's偉大的詩歌
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 請不要針對誰來講鐘聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩名為 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	內容是: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我也參與著人類的活動 , 不去問別人的鈴聲 , 反而是為此付出 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰.多恩 , 一個道德的建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 等同我們的生存 ,
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到延長壽命和健康的路徑 , danbuetner和團隊在研究世界上的 「 藍色慢活區 」 , 這些社區的長者和維姆住在一起 , 來記錄年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他共享9個常見的飲食習慣和生活方式 , 使他們持續地過一百歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到一百+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個叫做丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實 , 平均人類壽命長短只有百分之十 , 在某些生物限制下 , 是由我們的基因所決定的 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由我們的生活方式決定 ,
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能想出一個實際的公式來延長壽命
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的方程式是什麼 , 他們大概看不出來 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法或阿金減肥法
you have the usda food pyramid .	有美國農業部的食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 ,
there is what doctor oz tells us .	歐茲博士告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事情的真相是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的真相讓我們感到困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	說到營養品 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白葵呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	並且有目的性地參與其中嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	心靈層面 ? 及我們如何與人交流 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理上的定義
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 請一組專家到那裡來 , 用方法來做這些人的做法 , 提煉出跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	在結束後我會告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想先揭穿一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你努力工作 , 可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國的5000人中 , 只有一個活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常的低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題在於我們不是被設定為長壽的
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是被設為一種叫做 " 成功 " 的機制
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學的日子
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把這個名詞稱為 「 成功意味著你有孩子的年齡 」 , 然後再下一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在這種進化的效應完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠或是大象 , 或人 , 在這兩者之間 , 則是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要到一百歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得在基因樂透中勝利 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是:有治療方法可以幫助緩慢、反轉、甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有九十九件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	把你的腦袋剝奪氧氣僅僅幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就不會再復發 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太激烈 , 膝蓋的軟骨也跟不上軟骨
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用血小板衝上來 , 而我們可以得知阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , t.的兆個 , 我們在談的是國家債務總數 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會轉一圈 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次翻身都會有一些損壞 。 這樣的損害會增強 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數級的方式增加
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們都有披頭四或老鷹合唱團的日子我們在錄音帶上複製這段錄音帶讓朋友複製這個錄音帶 , 很快地 , 代代相傳錄音帶就聽起來像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個六十五歲的人老化的速度比一個十二歲的人快一百二十五倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼辦法可以減緩老化或停止老化 , 我到底在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上最厲害的科學告訴我們人體的能力我的身體 , 你的身體大約可用九十年女人的身體
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以這條線的某處我們只剩下大約十二年的美好歲月
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 他們多年來大多沒有慢性病、心臟病、癌症、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要把這些消失的時代 , 最好的方法 , 就是看看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷的文化 , 人們活到一百歲的比率 , 比我們大上十倍 , 平均壽命預期多出十幾年 , 中年死亡率應該會是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍寶地在義大利海岸外約一百二十五英哩處 , 薩丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 位於高地上 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們看到的是男人最長壽的百歲人瑞 , 比我們在美國的百歲人瑞多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還活得精彩 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十多歲的小夥子
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實可以回溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是個與世隔絕的青銅文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的不孕 , 它們主要是牧羊人 , 那裡有一些場合是規律的 , 低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主特別是以他們能帶到田裡的食物為主
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做carta , 用硬生麥做成的起士 , 用草原餵養的動物製作的乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自穀物餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 它的多酚物質含量比世界所知的任何酒都高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但是我認為真正的秘密 , 在於他們如何組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時就到頂點了 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 越年長你得到越多平等的 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只對你的老化父母有益 , 能讓他們和家人保持距離──他們有4到6年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 這也對那些家庭的孩童有益──他們有較低的死亡率和較低的疾病發生率 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	那叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了我們的第二個藍寶地 , 在東京南方 , 大約800英里 , 位在琉球的群島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而主島的北端 , 這張圖則是世界長壽的原點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是現存最老的女性群體 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有著世界上最長而無障礙的預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們能活很久 , 通常在睡眠不足時死亡 , 非常快速 , 通常 , 我能告訴你 , 在做愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	比美國人平均壽命長七年
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞的數量
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	得結腸癌和乳癌的比例是五分之一 , 美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	而心血管疾病率的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化所得的事實很明顯地表示他們有東西可以教我們
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為主的飲食 , 裡面全是帶有顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們吃大約八倍多的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起吃什麼 , 吃什麼比吃什麼更重要
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略要避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的幾個策略:他們會從較小的盤子下吃飯 , 所以在每個座位吃的卡路里也較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其照顧家庭風格 , 你說話時 , 可以無意識地吃 , 他們會在櫃台服役 , 把食物拿走 , 然後把食物送到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千年的格言我認為是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	由孔子所發明
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那飲食就是大家所知的騷擾 , hatchi , butchi
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在用餐之前說的一句話 , 提醒他們吃的時候 , 吃的就是80分飽了 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	飽足感要花半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住吃到八分飽就好能幫助你免於做這事
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 如薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構能讓我們聯想到長壽 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會害死人 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只有1.5個 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你可以生在琉球你會生在這樣的體系裡讓你自動擁有半打朋友陪著他們度過人生
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為模合 。 如果你處於某個模合走運時被期望分享優勢 , 如果你的幸運情形很糟 , 孩子生病、父母去世 , 你總是會有某個人負責 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個 「 模合 」 , 這五個女士相處在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是一百零二歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作、有生產力的地方 ,
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 碰 , 我們退休
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這代表要退休去使用簡單的椅子 , 或是下到亞利桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	相反的 , 有一個詞彙佔了你一生 , 那個詞是 「 ikigai 」
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大致翻譯: 「 早上起床的理由 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道師父來說他的生存價值就是拿著這位武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週捕三次魚 ,
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	而這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際給了我們一份問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	而其中一個問題 , 是文化上非常敏銳的 , 是那些問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生存價值只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩分別在一百零一歲半的時間裡
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著曾曾孫女的曾曾曾孫女 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回來 , 說: 「 感覺就像躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這想法很棒 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我找到美國的藍寶地 ,
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們去看明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡的百歲人瑞的比例非常高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的國家是基督復臨安息日會的基督徒集中在加州的羅馬林達市附近 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的衛理公會教徒
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	慶祝他們在星期五日落日的安息日 , 直到星期六日出 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱此為 「 二十四小時的避難所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	並且他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相對來說 , 是傳達他們非比尋常的壽命 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國這裡 , 女性的平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一個基督復臨派的女教友 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	斯特林研究中心我想它可以直接說明這個藍色慢活區計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個多種族的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲裔、
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套生活小習慣他們一生中大部份時間都習慣於儀式性地跟隨
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經中拿出他們的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十二九節上帝談到豆子和種子另一個是談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個避難所 ,
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時不管有多忙 , 工作壓力多大孩子都需要被推動去停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教的那一刻 , 都是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種權力不是偶爾才完成的 , 權力是一輩子每週完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往跟其他教徒來往
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的聚會 , 你不會看到人們在搖擺吉姆beam或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在說下一次的自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響著彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的人
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁可是當包商要求六千美金來建造隱私的圍籬時他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我會自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他都在外頭鏟水泥 , 把柱子拖來拖去 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料 , 也許在第四天他會被送進手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人而是做開心手術的人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲的他仍然每個月做20個開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上才開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 扔出公雞尾酒 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她孫子其實就住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	每天開始舉重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年的 「 安迪拉克 」 中 , 進入了她的 「 安德迪拉克 」 名字 , 被關在聖博納迪諾州高速公路上 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加十九次冒險活動 ,
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一你見過的人當中 , 騎著他的腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠並沒有防曬霜的那個人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有比和馬奇•戴頓合作 , 更恐怖的冒險了 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒遇到的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三個文化裡有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼呢 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	而我們成功的把它歸結為九項
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後我們又進行了兩次藍色地帶遠征 , 並且這些共同點依然適用 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	而第一個 , 我快要說了 , 這裡沒有一個是運動 , 至少是我們認為運動的方式 。
