instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們安排自己的生活 , 這樣他們就不斷被推展出身體的活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人她們坐在地板上 , 起身又坐下一天三、四十回
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	並沒有一個按鈕要去做院子工作或家務 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想攪拌奶油 , 他們會用手
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里跟跑步機一樣多
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們進行刻意的身體活動時 , 這是他們所享受的東西 。 他們傾向行走 , 這是唯一證實能延遲認知能力的衰退 , 而他們往往都有個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式安排他們的生活 , 所以他們有對的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都花時間在降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 7號基督復臨派教徒祈禱
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人敬祖
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕時間或壓力大時 , 會引發一種 「 發炎反應 」 , 這種反應跟很多病相關 , 從老年癡呆症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢個十五分鐘 , 你就會把那個發炎狀態變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	它們有詞彙來形容人生的意義 , 像是琉球人的 「 使命感 」 、 「 伊基加 」 ,
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道自己生命中最危險的兩年是出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率還有退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感 , 並在生活中活躍起來 , 那價值大約是七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點 , 沒有硬賣給美國的人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們往往以植物為主的飲食習慣
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是吃很多豆類跟堅果
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略保持過度飲食 , 一些小事在對的時間將他們推離桌面 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一照顧好孩子與年邁父母
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 這價值四到十四年額外的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做一次四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	其中最嚴重的是他們也屬於右派部落
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	不是出生便生 , 就是積極地與對的人圍繞在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕的研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機率會變超重
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人來往 , 隨著時間 , 會有很明顯的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點酒 , 但不多 , 他們吃得正當 , 他們吃得正當 , 而且他們信任和值得信賴 , 那將會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	節食是沒有用的 。 世界歷史上沒有一種飲食對超過2%的人口是有用的 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始 , 通常都是十月完成 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽命 , 不論是吃什麼 , 都沒有短期的解決方案 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但 , 想想看 , 你的朋友都是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最有意義的事 , 就是在生命中增加更多年 , 活到生命中去 。 謝謝大家 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水來導電 ; 一扇窗由清晰轉變成不透明的窗口 ; 一個可以產生音樂的果凍 。 所有這些東西都有的果凍 , 加泰娜莫塔說:該是玩的時候了 。 莫塔帶我們來一趟驚喜又酷的新素材之旅 , 暗示我們要知道它們有什麼用途 , 去實驗、修補、有趣的 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔琳娜.莫塔:玩弄智慧型材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機搭了一台車讓他可以運送家人
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做既是因為沒錢買車也是因為他知道如何建車
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一次我們了解到東西是如何運作的 , 了解它們是如何製作的 , 所以我們能夠建造、修理它們 , 或至少知道要買什麼的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多diy的做法自二十世紀下半葉起失傳
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群以及開放模型正將東西的運作及其成份帶回我們生活中而我相信我們需要更進一步去了解事物的組成
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統材料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚嘆又有未來感的複合材料塑膠能夠改變形狀 , 能導電的顏料、會改變顏色的顏料、會發光的布等 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不需要用傳統印刷電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小例子 , 我們用它來製造一個觸控感應器 , 透過打開這個小光就能感應我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家一直都在使用導電油墨 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上面 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光 , 但當我開燈時 , 整個表面都會有不同的光彩 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料有兩個已知的應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個東西放在一個裝在溫度的高溫板上 , 只比環境溫度稍高一點點 , 你就能知道會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個主要應用是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中的其它東西 , 所以它指出內容物是否涼了可以喝了 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	以上只是一些我們所知的智慧型材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	再過幾年 , 它們就會出現在我們日常所使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車但我們能有能隨著溫度改變顏色的牆壁有著可以捲起來的鍵盤式鍵盤還有在開關上變得不透明的窗口
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對東西的運作和製造方式感到好奇 , 也是因為我相信我們應該要對構成我們世界的元素有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些將建構我們未來的高科技的組成成成成成分了解還不夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	對於如何使用它們 , 幾乎沒有什麼可取得的資訊 , 且很少人知道它們是如何生產出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 現在 , 他們幾乎都存在在這個貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , 我和克絲蒂•波義耳開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為材料公開 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個我們 , 任何其他人想要加入我們的網站 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵他人隨時都可以貢獻 , 並聚集研究資源 , 像是研究論文和輔導 , 由其他像我們一樣的製作者所組成 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能變成一個大型、集體生成的資料庫 , 以便在智能材料上做diyourourf的資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料的運作方式以及組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 最後我們卻無法理解和使用塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 穿的衣服住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該去認識並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是創新總是由修補匠推動而來
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 而不是專家 , 一直是發明家和改進者 , 範圍從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但不見得總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩位科學家 , 很清楚這一點 , 當他們發表一篇論文時 , 用比較簡單的方法來製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克在那之前完全沒有相關化學經驗 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的自造物間複製實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據其他科學家的說明書自製試管震盪器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來將結果發表在網路上 , 包含他已經嘗試過的所有東西 , 且沒有成功的結果 , 讓其他人可以去研究並進行繁殖 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 喬登創新的主要形式是把實驗創造在設備相當的大學實驗室 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現 , 只用很便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己變成了 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿到他所離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的流程 , 改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提她的專案計畫是強調材料的表達特質同時著重建造者的創意和技巧
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子零件非常強大 , 他們能教我們物件如何運作 , 但設計上的限制與生俱來也會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的作法 , 另一方面 , 是創建一系列的技術 , 用來創造出不尋常的物品 , 來解放我們不受限於設計本身的限制 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 在漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗之中 , 這是我最喜歡的之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3播放器和一個磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜用各式各樣的材料製作出一系列的紙喇叭從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布及油墨
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登以及許多其它的製作者漢娜把她的食譜公開讓任何人都可以複製、繁殖
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有希望的材料科學其中一個分支 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜、靈活的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以 , 漢娜的手工藝工作 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 開啟一系列新的可能性 , 既具美感又有創新性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們的熱情和好奇所創造出來的 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們通常從非傳統的角度來處理問題 , 過程中 , 會發現其他的選擇 , 甚至是更好的做法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人在材料上做實驗 , 越多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務眾人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像泰德尼爾森在一九七零年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 現在你必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大架構 , 甚至沒有人夢想到家裡能有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡說得有點奇怪 , 「 你們現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要記住 , 取得關於新興科技的先發知識是確保我們在創造未來能有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃圈 , 鎖定門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來指引我們 , 即使我們只能看見前方和後方的車輛 。 但是如果汽車可以彼此分享它們的位置和速度 , 並且使用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路徑 ? 珍妮佛•赫利想像一個沒有發生意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但現實中 , 宗教偶像和運氣好的魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而百分之七十五的車禍和毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定說出任何一場意外 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	當時我還年輕在高速公路上 , 前面的車輛 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在停車 , 停車 , 在高速公路上停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只不過將65比0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我猛踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感受到abs的踢步 , 車子還在前進 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 而氣囊部 , 車子全部被截肢 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車會停我認為我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 只要讓我們的車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望大家回想一下現在開車的體驗 ,
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上車 , 關上門 , 你在一個玻璃泡內
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的軀殼裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在看不清路面的情況下在其他金屬巨人之間穿梭在超高速行駛的道路上
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	可以嗎 ? 你只需要引導你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你唯一擁有的 , 眼睛不是設計來做這個任務的 , 但後來有人請你做類似的事情 , 你想要換條車道 , 他們問你的第一件事情是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把眼睛從路上移開 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你前進的方向 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開下車不去看你目的地 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和所有其他人 。 這是安全駕駛的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我是要看這裡還是那裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會在路上做一個很棒的撿撿貨和選擇 ,
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們感知錯了或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我也相信這一點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能觀看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子之間會互相交換數據 , 我們不僅可以看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 左邊 , 左邊 , 全部 , 同時間 , 鳥瞰視線 , 我們甚至可以看到這些車子的影像 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能夠看見前方的車速 , 看看那傢伙開得多快或停下的時間 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人降到零分 , 我就會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何能預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是 。 有汽車 , 不是不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是立體的物體 , 有著固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	沿著道路行駛
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預備出版的路線上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來在哪裡 , 真的沒那麼難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在你的車上 , 和某個摩托車手過來了 ! 以85英里的時速 , 車道正式起飛 , 我知道你有這個經驗 , 並不是 「 無中生有 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙可能在路上開了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	是吧 ? 我是說 , 有人看過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10哩前20哩前30哩前 , 有人看到那傢伙 , 一車一看見那傢伙 , 就把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 地圖上估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你就會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那台車會在他耳邊小聲竊竊 , 像是: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車手 , 小心 ! 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測汽車的行為
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對牠們很好 ,
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 就像在汽車之間分享我們車與車之間的位置資料 , 單純地分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車上裝有gps和攝影機 , 我就能精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我有多快到哪裡 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估算我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 可以算是哪裡去了 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車輛也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以準確地知道自己身在何方也能模糊地看待其他車子的位置
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子分享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會如何 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以確切地告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了一個電腦模擬看下列情況會發生什麼事當用輕微的方式來估計當汽車只要分享gps資訊我們將這研究從電腦模擬中推進進到裝有汽車的機械試驗機上也就是現在裝在車子裡的機械感應器像是:立體攝影機、gps還有平面雷射雷射雷射雷射測量這些都是常見的備用備用系統
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的通訊錄 , 機械人彼此聊天 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器朝向對方靠近時 , 它們能追蹤到彼此的精確位置 , 且能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你過於聊天 , 很難處理所有封包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 而這就是預測模型會幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤可預期的軌道 , 你不會把注意力放在那些封包上 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	把那位看起來有點偏差的傢伙排在首位 ,
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	就可以預測新的軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了 , 你也知道怎麼了 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪些駕駛要提高警覺 , 才能脫身 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼樣警告所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲的說: 「 你得趕緊走 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 車子的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人擁有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們用手機 , 或 , 你知道的 , 做某一件事 , 他們可能不會在緊急時刻做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	因此 , 我們開始一條獨立的研究專門做驅動的狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三部攝影機 , 我們就可以偵測到駕駛在看向前看 , 看下面 , 看下手機 , 或是喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以預測誰、哪一部車是最好的車位以離開這條路去為每個人規劃最安全的路線
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技在現今的存在 ,
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願分享數據 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是個非常令人不安的想法 , 認為我們的車子會監視著我們 , 跟其他車子說說 , 我們會在一片流言密語的大海中沿著這條路往下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我對你不太了解 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們背後討論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請各位考慮一下一會兒 , 如果你真的不想要讓人分心的青少年在身後 , 才知道你要煞車 , 知道你要停下來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到對每個人最好的一件事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	來讓你的車八卦你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得.戴曼迪斯談到他是如何協助史蒂芬霍金實現他登上太空的夢想:飛到上層大氣層時 , 體驗到零g時的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短、講話、空間、科技、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬霍金的小彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金上任意轉變為零grogro 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我對開創太空新領域有多麼熱衷
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是在基因學archonxprize的場合上 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們正在進行的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在十天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因組-100個我們用來定序的個人 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特是那個活動的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你體重為零 ,
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他當場說: 「 沒錯 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要體驗zerog的唯一方法事實上是用拋物線飛行 , 沒有重量飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你乘坐飛機 , 飛過頂部 , 每25秒就沒有重量 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的體重是一倍高 ,
you do it again and again .	一而再 , 再而三地做
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得知八到十分鐘的無重力經驗美國太空總署訓練的太空人這麼久
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了十一年才營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	然後我們宣布將要搭載史蒂芬•霍金 ,
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關及飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想要去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了記者會 , 我們宣佈我們打算要做一個無重力拋物線飛行 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切進行得非常順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他 , 為什麼他要爬上去做這個 ?
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感動
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著不斷增加的危機被災難所消滅...
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果人類不上太空 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他去甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車內 , 坐落到zero-g飛機後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們總共有大約20個人捐款我們募集了15萬美元作為兒童慈善事業之用他們與我們同行
a few tedsters here .	這裡幾位tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生 , 及兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他血液的po2值、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急事件發生時 , 我們都已擁有一切 ; 天知道 , 你不會想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降 , 降落在那裡 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的夥伴byronlichtenberg跟我小心的把他懸在一塊
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到了那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 然後我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實讓一顆漂浮著的蘋果發揮在對艾薩克•牛頓爵士的敬意 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋也舉辦了同樣的椅子 , 那是艾薩克•牛頓爵士所做的 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這個人看上去並不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一顆珍貴的寶石上 , 而且是在我們有生之年 , 正要離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們 , 參與這場壯舉般的冒險之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky所呈現的3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現的是細胞內的動作 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•布林斯基對一個細胞進行動畫 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學繪圖師 , 我的觀點和別人稍微不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 以及科學中真與美的表現方式 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	儘管這些都是他們自身美妙的事物它們都有非常美妙的事物將它們導向真實與美麗可被科學與數學所檢視的事物就像是理想的連體兩人約會對象的雙胞胎
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是 「 真 」 的表示表示敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 , 不可或缺的
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨特的、有用的有時候 , 通常是很久以後 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你們可以翻幾張照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美往往對不在科學界的人而言才是事實和美麗 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	對於美的描述 , 通常只有在你了解了那些語言以及研究對象時 , 才會用到的語法和語法來描述那些真實與美麗的人 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙的常數 , 那裡有著人類的理想 , 你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字演化而來 。 這些是非常難以理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當醫學插圖師的經驗以來 , 我一直試著要做的事 , 從我被教導動畫的時候 , 我的父親是一位雕塑家 , 我的視覺導師 , 我想找出一種方法 , 協助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫、使用照片、說故事 , 讓人們不見得有證據能夠帶給人看 , 且能夠被傳授、了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一種環境中 , 在那裡 , 學生所學的主題 , 有著真與美的事物 , 但他們被教導的方式是分層式的 , 且被牽扯到的重點是真與美並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這就像是雞湯的陳年食譜 , 雞肉煮雞肉直到香味通通散去 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對待學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開啟教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話幾年前 , 他問我我和我的團隊是否有興趣真正改變哈佛大學的醫學與科學教育程度
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 它可以探索分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 讓學生能夠了解到一個他們可以掛在所有這些事實上的大圖片 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們腦海裡的細胞影像是一個由微機械所組成的大型、繁忙、複雜的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械正是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是奈米技術人員在世界各地所羨慕的 , 它們是自我引導的 , 強大的 , 精確的 , 精確的儀器 , 它們是由胺基酸所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械會驅動細胞的移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞複製、激發我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們力量了我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 想辦法把這個故事製作成動畫 , 它是哈佛大學biovisions的主軸 , 它是一個哈佛大學針對它的分子和細胞生物學系學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有文字資訊 , 除了過去式的物品之外 , 所有東西都可以視覺化 , 這樣這些學生們就有了內視覺化的觀點 , 對於細胞的真與美 , 能夠深入了解到他們腦中的真理 , 能激發他們腦中的想像力 , 如此一來 , 能運用他們腦中的靈魂 , 來進行探索 , 探索 , 探索 , 發現 , 發現 , 探索他們腦中的靈魂的原理 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子的組合方式 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作:你有巨噬細胞在微血管上流過 , 它們觸碰到微血管細胞壁的表面 , 它們在取出微血管壁上的細胞 , 它們被發送出了這個訊息 , 外面有發炎的訊息 , 在那裡 , 它們看不到也感知不到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的信息使他們停止 , 使他們內化 , 使他們必須做出各式各樣的零件 , 使他們改變形狀 , 試著脫離這微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛大學的科學家合作並與資料庫模型一起在原子上精確的分子並搞清楚它們是如何移動 , 並搞清楚它們所做的
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並想出如何以真理去做這件事情 , 藉由它導入了正在發生的事情 , 但不是這麼真實 , 以致細胞中密切擁擠的程度 , 能預防這種景觀的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我現在要給你們看的是我們製作的這個影片的第一部分的三分鐘讀者版 。 這是一個持續的計畫 , 將要進行四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這一點 , 看看細胞製造這些走路的路徑這些小機器叫做驅動蛋白 , 它們會拿這些巨大的負荷來挑戰相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請繼續看這部電影
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器是非常驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造它在果蠅身上所需的零件 , 從而透過閱讀基因的分子而來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 若沒有這些小小的微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯在這裡出席是非常零散的 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex快遞小組 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他把一大袋新製造出來的蛋白質拉到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜上 , 不論是對細胞膜 , 不論是對細胞膜 , 不論是對製造或是修補 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西可以跑來跑去 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞當中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家後 , 我希望你能想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到的一些關於細胞機械的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了所有發生了什麼事 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦知道發生了什麼事 , 我們將能真正地控制我們對健康所做的事 , 能用未來世代做的事 , 以及我們將來會活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能藉此發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們能夠意識到細胞在它們之間有什麼需要 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們會一起努力 , 它們會讓細胞執行它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起合作 , 幫助我們的身體──巨大的實體──它們永遠無法察覺它們的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請繼續欣賞接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓在她的貨車上規劃了一年 , 看到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱裝成一份自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅行變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事等 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家也是記者 , 我也是個非常有好奇心的人 , 所以在22年 , 身為記者 , 我學會了很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學會做一件事 , 就是當個隱世人 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了在職無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作 , 就在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的去世對我打擊很大 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事的時候 , 有很多事情會讓我感覺和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我這一生都在露營我決定在旅行車中生活一年就像一趟漫長的露營旅行
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓、我的洛威爾和我的露營裝備塞進了1975年的雪佛蘭小貨車上 , 開車到日落裡 , 完全沒有發現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:那社會把生活在一個永久的架構中 , 甚至是一個小木屋 , 作為一個人 , 有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到別人的負面看法會多快影響我們現實 , 假如我們容許的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	剛開始 , 住在旅行車裡很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 我定期在外用餐
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間休息和哀悼
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 關於我父親的死亡 , 憤怒和沮喪開始了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	自由工作結束了 。 我必須找全職來支付帳單
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天卻轉變為極熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	更不可能停車場 , 更不用說我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗來回地走
the doggy went into doggy day care .	道奇隊進入日間護理中心
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能做到時 , 我就把員工淋浴設在辦公大樓裡 , 卡車會停 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共休息室沖洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫下腐壞 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰塊在數小時之內就融化了 , 而且還蠻悲慘的 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起找到一間公寓 , 或是買不起可以讓我擁有羅特威爾和貓的公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	而我拒絕放棄他們所以我繼續待在旅行車裡
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當夜間的高溫讓我連走50英尺外的公共洗手間 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度降到零度以下 , 還留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我又面臨了一系列新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不同的地方 , 避免被警察注意到 , 被警察抓住 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺失控了我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個才華橫溢的作家和記者 , 變成一個住在車裡的無家者 , 把我吸氣的空氣帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒變 , 我的智商沒降低
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的正直、我的價值觀、關於我的一切 , 都還是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我卻是以某種方式改變了
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪中旋轉得更深、更深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊中人一樣臭又沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或喝得高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家可歸的人發現 , 包括一個以前的大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 你為何落得如此下場 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者沒有把我當成無家者但我有看到
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽到我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你抱有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的憂鬱症一個反應 , 讓我有了自殺傾向 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺了 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久後 , 有個朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯一個全國著名的記者 , 她在全國廣播電視節目上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 就在他死前一年 , 在提姆的新書上 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做一個講稿的節目迴路 。 他在說我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到timrussert , 與媒體會面的前主持人 , 當時我在一輛車裡住在沃爾瑪超市的停車場 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為到那時 , 我是個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那 , 重新讀一次我的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是一個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在旅行車上和朋友住在家鄉的沙發上做交替 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又重新開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	第二年夏天 , 我是一名工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	當時我正獲獎 , 住在我自己的公寓裡
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬人全職工作兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化並將生活在車上或街上犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 遊民、工作無家者 , 主要還是保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 讓他們投入 , 鼓勵他們 , 給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的心靈可以克服一切有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家者的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵各位 , 把錢給下一個乞討者 ,
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們的居住地不是他們的住處 , 而是睡在哪裡 , 或是人生中的狀況隨時都在發生什麼 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪超市的停車場內而今天我在ted演講
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶我們走過全國的大膽計劃 , 從1970年代開始 , 提高人們的生活水準 。 第一步是:人口控制 。 那就表示 , 許多法蘭克 , 有趣的 , 和非常有效的談論關於保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	米奇亞維拉瓦迪亞:保險套讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定針對此點下手 , 但我們不是從福利方案開始 , 也不是貧窮減少計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭規劃開始 , 遵循非常成功的母親產婦健康活動 , 一系列活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以 , 基本上 , 沒有人會接受計畫 , 如果孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以第一步:先去找孩童 , 去找母親 , 然後再進行家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 1974年也是如此 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有七個孩子都有很大的成長率 , 比例是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們就說: 「 就去做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們也同意 , 我們會用避孕藥 , 但我們需要醫生來幫我們開藥 。 」 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有選擇 「 不 」 的答案 , 而是以 「 不 」 的形式 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 在解釋如何使用避孕藥上做得很棒 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很棒 , 但這只佔了全國20%的面積 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人怎麼做 , 讓他們一個人孤單 , 說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找了那些你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	實際上 , 在那個黃色標誌下 , 我希望他們還沒被消滅 , 因為那時有 「 可口可樂 」 存在 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時我們比可口可樂還大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們所選的人是我們所選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己做家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	這樣他們就可以供應藥丸和保險套 , 遍及全國各地 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們在那裡 , 被視為問題的起因的人 , 去解決問題 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論有多少人 , 你都可以看到有船和婦女 , 販賣東西--這裡是浮動市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 何不讓宗教信仰 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很堅強 , 而泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那邊是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗聖水 , 讓和尚把聖水灑在避孕藥和保險套上 , 供給家人神聖的神聖 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳遍了整個國家 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 ,
it's been blessed . "	它是有福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們找上教師

so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們 ,
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	有超過25萬人在課本上課 , 關於節育計畫的新字母--a , b是生育 , c是保險套 , i是子宮節育器 , v是輸精管切除 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 讓你投擲骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你停在任何應有的規劃上 , 你就往前走了 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥片 ,
very good , mother . move ahead .	很好 , 媽媽 。 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	舅舅買保險套 。 非常好 , 舅舅 , 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	舅舅喝醉了 , 沒有用保險套 。 回來 , 再開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育 , 階級娛樂
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做了這些 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有使用保險套的接力賽道 , 有著兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久後 , 保險套就被稱為女孩子的好友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮苦人家來說 , 鑽石不會變成所以保險套才是女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出微型貸款計畫 , 組織計畫的婦女說: 「 我們只想借錢給有執行節育計畫的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 就照顧好懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	這也是他們所經營的
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36 , 還在持續著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村子發展銀行的一部分 ; 不是真的銀行 , 只是小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來運作它自己也是由村民自己來運作
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	在那裡你可能很難看到一個泰國男子 , 總有女人 , 女人 , 女人 , 女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	後來我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每一個人 , 無論他們是否願意幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供輸精管切除術 , 但尤其是 , 排隊前面的美國人 , 排隊前面的是大使館的住宅 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給了我們一間球場 , 非常適當的場地 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	正因為接近午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們來點午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 那一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你會得到兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物變成漢堡或熱狗二選一 。 "
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我也認為熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	接下來是這位年輕人 , 名叫威利.博 , 他替美國國際開發總署工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯的 , 他得了輸精管切除術 , 因為熱狗的一半被吃掉了 , 他非常高興 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 同時也激怒了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 。 過來吧 , 我會幫你們全部人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	所有這一切 , 從7個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5個 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你也可以稱它為可口可樂法 , 如果你喜歡它是一模一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂跟隨我們 , 還是我們追隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	所以每個人都要加入這個行列 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強勢政府 , 沒有很多醫生
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但是每個人的工作 , 能夠改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來到了泰國 , 我們得要停止做許多好事來對抗愛滋病 。

so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以 , 我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊吧 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去拜訪了軍方 , 要求借用300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的槍多過政府 , 而且擁有的槍也比政府多

and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	就在那時我們對著航空的波浪

and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校都有愛滋病的教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些高中生在教高中生 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最棒的老師是女孩子們 , 不是男孩 , 她們都很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些到處教導的女孩關於安全性愛和愛滋病毒 , 她們被稱為德雷莎修女 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再往下一步 ,
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級、四年級的孩子 , 去村子裡的每個家庭、在整個泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每一個家庭 , 給這些小朋友 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有家長反對因為我們試圖拯救生命這簡直是救命仙丹
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以 , 你也有公司發現 , 生病人員沒有用 , 消費者沒買 , 消費者沒買 。

and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們在街上發放保險套 , 不論在哪裡 , 任何地方都一樣 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	還有 , 在交通上 , 警察會給你保險套──我們的 " 警察與瓦礫 " 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察發給你保險套嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	當然我可以 。 他們非常享受這一切 。 我可以看見他們就站在一旁 , 無所不在 。

and then , new change , we had hair bands , clothing and the condom for your mobile phone during the rainy season .	接著 , 新的改變 , 我們有了毛帶、衣服 , 和你的手機保險套 , 在雨季時期 。
and these were the condoms that we introduced .	這些是我們推出的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	一個說 " 大規模防護性武器 "
we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現這裡有人在尋找大規模殺傷性武器 , 但我們已經找到大規模防護性武器:保險套 。
and then it says here , with the american flag , " don't leave home without it . "	然後它說 , 有了美國國旗 「 不要離家了 」

but let me warn you , these are thaisized , so be very careful .	但讓我先警告你們 , 這些是泰國化的 , 所以請小心點 。

why just run around ?	為什麼要跑來跑去 ?
and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 反之 , 我們說: 「 在橡膠上 , 我們信任它 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以 , 你可以看到我們把每樣東西加入我們的努力去讓人們的生活更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精很容易影響判斷 。
and then what happened ?	接著發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	經過這段時間 , 每個人都加入了
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國 , 愛滋病的新病例數量下降了90% , 根據世界銀行的統計 , 770萬人的生命因而獲救 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有多少泰國人到處走動 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	它只是顯示出 , 你可以對它做些什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	資金有90%來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	當時有政治承諾 , 一些財務承諾 , 每個人都加入了這個鬥爭 。
so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以不要只把它丟給專家、醫生、護士 。
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人民脫離貧窮 , 現在愛滋病有點脫節了 , 這次不是單獨的政府 , 而是和企業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧困的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 無法取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是商業社群提供的
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試圖將它們轉變為赤足企業家 , 小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法 , 就是透過商業企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 這件事完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司的經費從村子透過 「 樹木移植 」 ,
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植了樹木 , 錢種進了他們的小額貸款基金中 , 我們稱之為鄉村發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入了 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在能借這筆錢之前 , 你得要先被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧困中的人 , 信用能力必須要成為人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你必須先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	下面我們稱之為赤腳企管碩士 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 當他們借到錢時 , 就能成功運用這個生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 還有這個非常有趣的東西 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 。 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該不要再做鞋子和衣服了 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	做這些更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有泰國絲綢 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們製造蘇格蘭方格紋 , 就如你們左邊所見的 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭老人 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機也許感覺像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友 , 會偶爾給你微笑一下 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•瑞納多•狄摩 , 智慧型手機供電的mini機器人可以和你一起步行 , 為你滑行一杯咖啡 , 通過桌子 , 為你做出可編程表達的反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	凱勒.瑞諾:一個迷你機器人 , 用你的手機驅動它 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉一下手你們家中有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 事實上這兩隻手 , 如果你不包括roomba在家中有多少人有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們romotive公司想解決的問題我和其他二十位宅男都很著迷於解答
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想打造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不管你是八歲還是八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要做出一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 它不僅是真正負擔得起的 , 它還必須是人們真的想要帶回家並帶著孩子的機器人 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能是令人毛骨悚然或是不可思議的 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善又可愛的
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人是用你已熟知的設備來愛你的iphone當作它的大腦
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量我們可以創造一個連接wi-fi無線網路的機器人讓電腦視覺化它只花150塊美金這大概是過去這類機器人花費的百分之一
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他是在生物模式中
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上正在裝置上使用攝影機來跟蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我放下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很謹慎 , 所以他會一直盯著我 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我從這邊過來 , 他會轉向跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我從這邊過來--他很聰明
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--呃-哦 , romo累了--如果我想要和romo一起探索世界 , 我可以將他和任何ios的設備做連結 。

if i get in front of romo here .	如果我在這romo面前
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想控制他 , 我可以直接開車 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在任意兩個智慧型設備之間做雙向的音訊和影片 。

so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們之前談到遠端臨場感 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年只能見到她孫女一兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我最後想談談我們未來在努力的事情 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個稱為blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖曳這些段落的語義代碼 , 為這個機器人創造任何你想要的任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo行為模式 ,
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上你可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這些行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中去執行它 , 在現實生活中執行該項目 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	接著 , 如果你有什麼值得讓你驕傲的你可以和世界上每個擁有機器人的人一起分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些無線網路無線網路的機器人 , 實際上會互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們極度專注於建造一個大家都能訓練的機器人的原因 , 是因為我們認為 , 在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式 , 是針對個人機器人 。
they change from person to person .	人與人之間的改變
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你家中有個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己想像出來的具體實現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我根本不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 這不是10年或100億美金 , 也不是一個大型的類人型機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在今天 , 它會依靠小型、敏捷靈活的機器人 , 像romo那樣 , 以及像你們一樣的人所創造出來的 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們迫不及待地想把機器人全都送到你手上 , 我們迫不及待地想看看你打造了什麼東西 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和社會活動家伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然還有 , 這場演說中的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育子女、講故事、女性、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝•阿言德講述激情故事 ,
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常感謝 。 能站在這裡真是可怕 , 最聰明的人之一 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴各位幾個充滿熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一句猶太諺語說我很喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真實的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想傳達的是一個比真相更真實的傳達關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些甚至令我不感興趣 , 直到最後我把它們寫下來 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治及社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我注意到我們身邊的神祕感 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了一些書 , 但是我過著匿名的生活 , 直到2006年的2月 , 當我在義大利舉行奧運時 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在人們可以在梅西百貨公司認得我 , 我的孫子們覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	請讓我告訴你我的四分鐘名聲
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個籌辦奧運開幕儀式的籌辦人打電話給我說我被選為護旗者之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這一定是認錯人了因為我根本不是運動員 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定可走得完體育場一圈就沒有助行器
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是在笑 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	5位女性將分別代表5大洲另外還有3位奧運金牌得主
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說過一套制服 , 要求我量測
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一面遠景 , 穿著鬆軟的長褲 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中旬 , 我到了杜林 , 人群熱情歡呼時 , 80個奧運選手都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了一切去比賽 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的小東西 , 冰層的一英吋 , 風的力量 , 可以判斷出種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報上面印著奧運標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 不見得都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運的因素 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要 「 獨行俠 」 、 「 異議者 」 、 「 冒險家 」 、 「 局外人 」 、 「 反叛 」 , 他們會問問題、會改變規則、會冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 ,
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會做有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會是好前夫 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我見到其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊薩蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩位心中充滿熱情的女性來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主旺加里•馬塔伊她種植了三千萬棵樹 , 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤和天氣在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村莊的經濟狀況
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨行動派女子蘇曼麗•曼她熱誠地和兒童賣淫對抗
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 祖父將她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴這些人相信跟年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而這些妓院中 , 孩童被迫每天接收5位、15位客戶 , 如果孩子反抗 , 他們就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到制服的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的衣服 , 但這跟我原本想穿的米其林人裝很遠 , 真的很爛 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但是大部份的旗手也一樣 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 通用的象徵美麗與熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很瘦弱 , 很高 , 有很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能擁有一個深色的棕色 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視訪問中被問到: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼美好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直的 , 我也不會發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你有來自地球上最美麗的女性之一的免費建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有吼 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有吵鬧 , 沒有吵鬧 , 沒有和自己說話 , 沒有放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有說是真的 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在大約午夜的時候 , 我們被送到體育場的翅膀上 , 擴音機傳來了奧林匹克旗幟 , 開始的音樂是從這裡開始的 , 阿依達進行曲 。

she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿將旗子的一角舉在肩上 。 我則在後面小跑步抱著那支旗子 , 將旗子舉在我的延展手臂上 , 這樣我的頭其實是在該死的旗子底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的鏡頭當然是蘇菲雅

a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人都很想去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是那些在奧林匹克運動場上

i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我希望能將奧運的關鍵字刻在心中 ,
so here's a tale of passion .	所以 , 這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 該地方是剛果境內的圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和被迫遷移的人是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 會因疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子們
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 還懷了寡婦 。

somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這家人存活了16個月然後 , 靠著非凡的運氣和一名年輕男子薩夏•查諾夫他的熱情 , 讓她能夠進入美國救援機、蘿絲•瑪班多及她的九個孩子最後到亞利桑那州鳳凰城在那裡生活及成長茁壯
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中 , 代表偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且有熱情的女性 , 如蘿絲•瑪班多 。

the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	那個地方是孟加拉一個村莊的小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國潔牙師她到診所當義工當了她三週假期的時候
