they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水比男人的薪水低於男性同等薪水只要她們有薪水可領 , 她們仍然是弱者 , 因為她們沒有經濟獨立 , 且不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。

the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最落後的社會總是把女性放下來的那些社會

for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性相關計畫每得到1美元就有20美元提供男性相關計畫

in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷最多的都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女與兒童 。 他們是附帶傷害的 。

this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大多數人都在問的基本問題
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序有道理嗎 ?

in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份我看到費南多•巴特羅的畫展在博克萊大學圖書館

what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無罪的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力被濫用 , 以及權力被濫用 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖會定義現實 , 逼迫其他成員接受現實 , 遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在改變 , 但總能帶來好處 , 在這種情況下 , 沒用的 " 下滲效應 " , 在經濟上行不通的 , 效果完美無缺 。

women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩童 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最一無所有的男人也有人可以虐待一個女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數幾個通過性別、收入、種族和階級的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以從根本改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但若要真正改變 , 我們就需要女性的能量管理世界 。

old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是沒希望的 , 我們得要等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳說性的乳房
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願有位勇士心臟位在旺加里馬塔伊 , 索馬里的媽媽 , 珍妮 , 和蘿絲•瑪班多 。

not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是為了讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是可能的 。 看看四周--這些知識、活力、才華和科技
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們離開我們的風扇 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造出一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在一個和倫敦一樣大的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐點都在那裏 。 但是所有的食物從哪裡來 ? 卡洛林鋼商業討論每日的餵養都市的奇蹟 , 並展現古老的食物路線如何塑造了現代社會
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為如果我們走進一家商店或餐廳 , 或一小時之內進到這間戲院大廳 , 將會有食物等待著我們 , 神奇地從某處趕來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到倫敦這個大小的城市 , 每天就要有足夠的食物被製造、運送、買、賣、煮、吃、處置 , 類似的事情 , 每天都要發生在地球上的城市 , 都要有很了不起的食物 , 完全可以養活 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿牠們是世上最自然的東西 , 忘記了我們也是動物 , 我們也需要進食 , 實際上我們就像古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們愈來愈多進入城市 , 更多那種自然世界會被轉化為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀一樣──這是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景色非凡但少有人見識過
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而且越來越多的這些景觀並不只是用來餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們愈來愈多進入城市 , 更多人開始吃肉 , 所以 , 全球每年的穀物中 , 有三分之一都被餵食動物 , 而不是給我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	要花三倍的穀物 , 其實是十倍的穀物 , 要拿來餵飽人 , 如果是從動物身上穿過的話 , 那就不是很有效率的飼料了 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個越來越嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們有兩倍的人口住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	估計肉類和乳製品的消耗量也會增加兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市化的手提升
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 事實上 , 如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 這個問題是很不可能解決的 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們也失去相當於現存的可耕種的可耕地以獲取和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方世界每一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的熱量
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即使有我們用極大的成本在製造的食物 , 我們事實上並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	目前美國有半數的食物被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這個漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有辦法妥善餵飽這顆行星 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	有十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球百分之八十的食物交易只由五大跨國企業來控制時這是一個嚴峻的圖片
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們逐漸進入城市 , 世界也接受了西方的飲食習慣 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們展望未來 , 不穩定的飲食
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們怎麼會變成這樣 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼辦 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	為了回答稍微容易一些的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這是這個過程的開始 , 在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的肥沃地區的開始 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如同你所看到的 , 它是新月狀的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業 , 和城市主義大約在同一地點 , 同時發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市是緊密結合的 , 它們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們遠古祖先第一次發現的穀物可以造出足以支撐永久居住的食物來源
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些定居處是什麼樣子的 , 我們可以看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們的周圍有生產力的農地 , 並由像烏爾的這一個大型神廟所主宰 , 事實上 , 是神聖化的中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排農作收割收集穀物獻給諸神再把諸神沒吃的穀物獻給人民
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活 , 是由他們賴以維生的穀物和收成所主宰 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 這對每一個古老城市來說都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元一世紀時 , 羅馬有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市如何能提供食物給自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物里程數 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬得以進入海洋 , 使得它從很遠的地方運來食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這在古代唯一可行的方法 , 因為運送食物到道路上是非常難的 , 本來就相當艱難 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	而且食物很快就壞掉 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動了戰爭 , 像是有關卡瑟奇和埃及這些地區的戰爭 , 僅僅是為了取得他們的穀物存量 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 整個帝國的擴張真的是一個長期有軍事化的購物中心
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下羅馬還曾經是從倫敦進口牡蠣的一個階段.我覺得那是很了不起的
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬以它的食欲塑造它的內陸
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 其他事情也發生在工業化前的世界
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看17世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到 , 穀物是從泰晤士河運來的 , 沿著地圖下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場都位於城市的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路上引領人們走上廉價的道路 , 那是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字麵包街 , 你就能知道三百年前那裡發生了什麼事
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然對魚也是一樣的 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河裡來的 。 一樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	比林斯門是過去倫敦有名的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的是非比尋常 , 真的 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都帶著手機到處遊走 , 看起來像磚塊 , 還有種臭味的魚兒正從港口下來 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事一旦運輸到城市的根源就被建立起來 , 它們幾乎不會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類產品則是另一回事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉品來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它開始來了 , 抵達城市西北邊 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位於那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽是從東安格利亞進來的 , 再到東北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得我有點像氣象女子在做這個 。 總之 , 鳥兒也進來的時候腳上都很小的帆布鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當它們碰到便宜的東端時 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它叫做 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你去看任一城市的地圖在工業時代前就可追溯食物的來源
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你真的可以看到它是如何被食物實體塑造的 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名稱 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是買賣食物唯一的場所
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們回顧1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面你會發現居住在這樣一個城市裡很不容易得知你的食物從哪裡來
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜天的午餐 , 可能是三天前在你的窗外吹氣或在外面流血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 一個有機的循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西方國家的照片 ,
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你可以看到 , 最早的鐵路旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被奪去了視力和心智在鄉間的某處被屠殺
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並且用鐵路運進城裡 ,
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	一開始 , 它會讓城市第一次發展到任何大小、形狀、任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去 , 它們得要透過非常艱難的實體方式來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理上有效地解放了出來 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	各位可以從倫敦的地圖上看到 , 火車出現後的90年裡 , 從一個很容易餵飽的小斑點 , 由動物走進來的路徑 , 到一個很大的懸浮點 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 無論是動物 , 還是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車 , 這個標誌著這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放完全從任何與大自然的明顯關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這個城市是沒有氣味的 , 沒有混亂的 , 沒有人的本質 , 因為沒有人會夢想走進這樣的景觀中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了得到食物所做的是他們上了車 , 開到位於郊區的某處的箱子 , 帶回一週的購物 , 然後好奇地球上有什麼可以拿來用 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	在這個時刻 , 我們和食物、城市的關係 , 徹底改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	在這裡 , 我們有過去食物是中心 , 是城市的社會核心 , 位於周邊區域 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	過去是社會事件 , 買賣和賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 現在只需加水 , 或加點蛋糕 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物可吃的味道
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需把背包上的標籤讀取一小部分
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 , 也不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是珍視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統最諷刺的一點是他們已經把他們所承諾的要來讓事情變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉著它能夠在任何地方建立城市 , 實際上它們已經讓我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 也就是我們和自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	它們也讓我們依賴那些只有它們才能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續發展的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾就在問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的著作 " 烏托邦 " 的字首
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 聽起來有點熟悉 , 每天從彼此散步 , 人人基本上都是農田 , 在後園種植蔬菜 , 一起吃公共餐點 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的根本原則 , 儘管更像是未曾如此形容 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個著名的烏托邦遠景 , 埃本内則.霍華著的 " 花園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一連串的半自給自足的城邦 , 一小塊大都市裡有可耕地 , 一路連接另一塊地 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物也能被說成是他視覺的規則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	甚至還建好了 , 但和霍華的願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦概念的問題 , 它們是烏托邦概念的 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有希臘語的雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是指好地 , 或無地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的、想像的 , 我們無法擁有
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 做為一種概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不再有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了另一種選擇 , 希托邦 , 從古希臘文 , 希托 " 象徵食物 , 和 " 托波斯 " 的原意 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在 " 希托邦 " 中 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作是非常強大的工具──一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果要這麼做 , 希托邦可能會長得怎樣 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 。 只是狗臉上的表情 。

but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但 , 當然 , 那也不是個很棒的照片 , 因為我們得要再也不用做這樣的食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多想想多元文化 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖只為我概括了我們應該要做的思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是一種對食物塑造我們生活的方式的重新概念 。

weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	《慈悲憲章》的幾個星期後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯觀察了宗教在21世紀扮演的角色:它的教條會讓我們分裂嗎 ? 還是它會團結我們 , 是因為共同的利益 ? 她會檢視帶動世界信仰的催化劑 , 重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal9、暴力、
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新訂定黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為 , 身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心的核心 , 在所有主要的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都進化出自己的版本被稱為黃金法則
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它會出現一本正面的版本: 「 盡可能善待別人 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 " 己所不欲 , 勿施於人 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下都拒絕將這種痛苦加諸其它人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調的是同情心的重要性不只因為它聽起來很棒而且因為它很有效
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實行了黃金法則就像孔子說的 , 「 不分晝夜 」 這個問題不只是做善事 , 每天又回到貪婪、自私的生活 , 而是一整天都要做 , 把自己從世界的中心角度貶低 , 換到另一個 , 你也超越了自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	這會帶你進入所謂的上帝、涅盤、帶著你、rama、tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	一些超越我們所知的超越了我們在有限的自我存在的範疇 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活十分重要 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖會團結在一起 , 他們在爭論深奧的教義 , 或說出一連串充滿仇恨的議會 , 或煽動反對同性戀或類似的事 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	人們往往不太願意憐憫人
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士交談時 , 看到他們有著堅定的表達方式 , 橫越他們的臉 , 因為人們通常會希望自己是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	那我為什麼對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地帶領我離開我的書線研究 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠對在更廣大的觀眾演說 , 比我想像的還要寬廣 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這事很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們對待所有的人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 就好像他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有可行的世界要交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 這個時代的一個偉大任務 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如同我之前所說的 , 在這裡 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人物相信黃金法則 ,
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種同理心的想像行為 , 把你自己放在他人的處境 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調我們的信仰的教條或是不寬容的一面 , 或是回到拉比希爾 , 老的耶穌教徒 , 他被一個異教徒指責 , 用一個異教徒單腳站立他會說: 「 你不願為你的鄰居做什麼 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉和其他東西只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比和教會的早期父子們說 , 任何對經文的解讀只要培養出仇恨和鄙視 , 都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們必須復興這樣的精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛的精神喚醒我們而發生 ,
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切實現 , 我們能使用ted介紹的現代通訊做實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經為我們所有伴侶的回應感到無比振奮
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一組人要用 「 憲章 」 來療癒新加坡社會最近出現的分歧 , 議會的某些成員也希望在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 即將有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們知道同情心也在所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區舉辦了活動和討論 , 討論以慈悲為中心的議題 , 在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中都有 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它無法就此停止 , 發射不能就此停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教誨 , 在這裡 , 我們走錯了路 , 只聚焦於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨應該要付諸行動
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這直到死亡的日子工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續和我們的合作夥伴一起做兩件事──教育並刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經放棄了同情心 ,
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們經常認為這只代表對某人感到抱歉
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不會理解同情心如果你只是想一想
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們參與媒體的目的 , 是因為媒體在幫忙破除我們對其他人的一些刻板印象深刻的看法 , 這些觀點將我們彼此分離 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也同樣適用
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能夠感受到動力 , 動力和挑戰一種以同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它要求急性智慧 , 不只是一種可怕的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想請求學者們以他們自己以及他人的傳統探討同情心的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 鼓勵無情說話的積極性 , 這麼一來 , 因為有《慈悲憲章》 , 不管人們的信仰為何 , 或缺乏他們自身的權力 , 去挑戰那些不被熱情的言論 , 那些來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 那些來自產業界的頂尖領導者 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從沒想過把憲章放到網路上
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊的世界裡 , 一大群人坐在房間裡 , 發表另一個無人機的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted為我介紹了一種全新的思維方式以及發表構想 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這正是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識如果我們一起努力 , 我們就能改變這個世界
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有些時候 , 這些問題看似無關緊要 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但是我想引用一段話做結尾參考英國作家牛津的作者我不常引用c.s.路易斯
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話一直在我腦中揮之不去 , 打從我還是個學童時期開始 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四種愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視對方的眼神 , 咒罵對方的眼神 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這段感情與友情比較 , 當兩個人並肩站在一起 , 肩並肩 , 眼睛固定在一個共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 ,
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我非常強烈地感受到 , 在我們在維多利的小小使命期間 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起 , 肩並肩努力朝著共同目標努力 , 差異就會消失 。
and we learn amity .	我們也學會了雄心壯志 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起住 , 認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay對羅馬競技場有時甚至會有一種超現實的旅程這些旅程都向歷史城市致敬
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgrant , 藝術 , 藝術 , 藝術 , 書籍 , 城市 , 溝通 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事.
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫 , 是為了更好的了解事物
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我畫了很多卻還是不明白我在畫什麼
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	那些對數位產品感到自在的人 , 甚至是走私關係的人 , 可能會覺得有趣 , 知道那個關係最熟悉 「 事物運作的方式 」 的那個人 , 還要為 「 理解 」 做準備 , 花兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆電和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延伸管理人員
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我老是把我的延伸物管理好 , 所以連我自己也沒想過要看指示 , 但我終於找到解答了 , 因為接到邀請時 , 我嚇壞了 , 提醒我 , 沒有投影機 , 所以把那些屍體帶出來 , 不再有必要 , 反而是以另一種形式的溝通 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所知的事物 , 這種特別適合在座許多技術敏感的人 , 或是我可以談談我真正關心的事情 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定跟後者
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	我為什麼要特別在意羅馬 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在羅德島設計學院念建築的時候是在六零年代後期
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 在我當學生的最後一年 , 也就是第五年 , 在羅馬度過 。 這改變了我的一生 。

there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	藍色一排排排廢氣排出的油氣會貫穿這條小徑
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想 , " 等等 , 我在幹嘛 ? "
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只可以用整齊的方式收集和儲存資訊 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是會把一層剝掉我們會把他們當成一層頁面 , 用某種方式去做
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成是層層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個有層次地層次的地方 , 垂直地層次 。 我心想 , 如果我把它們剝成一頁頁頁 , 可以讓你用正確的方式呈現出這些層次的深度 ,
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬的建築物牆上大部份的黏土覆蓋著疤痕 ; 經過數個世紀的改變留在其適應之下而不是被拆掉 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你就會看到它背後的意思 , 叫做疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造小windows的必要性已經到了 , 因為壞人要來了 , 不論如何 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應作用都埋藏在工作樂園之下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以從這個palazzo的頁面向你展示它的內部狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我還可以給你們看它在某個很壯觀的建築物的角落裡有那些巨大的石塊 , 或是用磚頭和史多哥做的假石塊 , 比較常見的情況是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得有一點點的三維空間 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從一條狹小的街道中帶到其中一個令人訝異的廣場 , 用雙扇摺疊就可以摺出雙扇摺疊頁 。 如果你小時候跟我一樣 , 讀著彈出書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	把頭包起來 , 留在廣場上那短暫的時間 ,

ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書整個打開 , 如果我只把書打開九十度 , 我們就在俯視萬神殿的正前方 , 就有點像是頂部 , 或多或少處在廣場上 。

no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有什麼把戲 , 只是本書沒有完全打開 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這好像很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺疊和唯一的開本書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入了萬神廟內部 , 它會不斷成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我是走在正確的軌道上 , 但那有點失去了人性的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要引起人們注意到一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 這是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 令我印象深刻
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是一隻回家的鴿子 , 它會叫做 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個頭銜有用 , 使用它 。 但那會是一個穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示我對羅馬的喜愛 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子正坐在教堂的上面
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天就要掉下來做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方被鷹架和綠色網子覆蓋 , 而且這個鴿子不可能回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以這隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠將必須找到另一個棲身之處 , 這讓我能夠通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從最高的那些開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人住在一起 ; 這不一定是好事 , 但牠能再次將鴿子凝聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我當時想 , 這有點意思可是也許有個人應該以某種方式參與其中
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想到一個老傢伙他終其一生都在照顧生病的鴿子
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方去把他們弄危險 , 搞什麼不好 , 他們會和這個人變成朋友 , 學會幫他耍把戲 , 娛樂他 , 諸如此類的東西 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	存在著一個真實的聯繫 , 存在於這位老人與這些鴿子之間 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是他病了 , 病的很重
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天沒見到他之後有一天他住在一個小閣樓他們把他的名字拼寫在四周飛來飛去
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 一起爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有鴿子 , 一隻紅色的氣球 , 在那等著他 , 他們把他搬到城牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這件事:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會帶鴿子出城 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死者從未被埋在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個讓人愉快的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	真的要走很長的路
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷過...如果包裝沒有用 , 故事就沒用了 , 我就只是想出書名 , 希望書名能讓我朝著正確的方向前進 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它的確足夠讓我專心 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些頁面最終引領我找到了解決方案 , 故事是一位年輕女子傳來的訊息 , 她住在羅馬城外 , 傳到在城市中的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從阿婆利亞號上空飛過
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看見墳墓和松果 , 一路上看得到 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看見那條紅線 , 你看見鴿子的小徑 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得有必要而且可能 , 試著傳達出那種在城市中飛越時的感受 , 卻不去真正移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--這些你都很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 穿越大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的現象 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大多會讓鴿子們不會做的事:它走了趨勢線 , 這個裝置是我認為可以把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們環繞羅馬競技場 , 穿過希臘的聖母教堂 , 朝著河流的聖塔瑪利亞寺廟前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和法蘭基羅的飛行器是米開朗基羅所設計的石材 , 用羅馬競技場拆下來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯衝過坎博底特菲里族 ,
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給我的學生看的其中一件事因為這是完全雜亂的一種完全否定所有觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法就是只要看上去可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪 ; 有幾個就在火星上 , 另外幾位在克雷莫納 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進入廣場 , 在和平聖母堂前面 , 在那裡 , 無時無刻都有一場足球比賽在進行 , 我們被足球給擊中了 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球擊中的一個恐怖的畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有各式各樣的片段:和平聖母堂 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀的一小部分 , 什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看清楚很平聖母堂--像這樣的書很靈活 , 很互動--只要把它轉過來 , 再以另一種方式看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到撞擊紅線所造成的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥把自己拉向中世紀的塔樓--其中一個塔中世紀剩餘的中世紀塔樓 , 走向聖依諾的教堂 , 周圍的圓頂向下俯瞰著廣場 , 我們已經提到並飛過了好幾次 , 這裡有四條河流的伯尼雕像 , 接著穿過了很棒的聖詩集 , 停下了很長的直徑26英尺 , 停在我們用來紀念的天堂上 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面到處跑 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們不用在這個特定的時刻擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以在紙上以任何方式朝向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	飛過gesu時 , 飛得有點激動這並不讓人意外
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	從我剛剛談到的 " 雕刻美麗的牆壁 " 中有我提到的 " 新興作品 " 標誌 , 和 " 美麗的雕刻品 " 標誌 , 以此類推 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到了palazzo的前庭也就是目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院進入閣樓 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上畫畫 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	牠把訊息從鳥的腿上移開 ; 牠是這麼說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	我們看看畫板邊 , 可以看到牠正在製作的事實上 , 是鴿子飛行的路線圖 , 紅色的線穿過所有視覺影像 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員關於自行組合的想法--與其創造一些東西 , 我們可以創造一些材料 , 成為一股dna自行組合的方式 。 它是一個在初期階段很大的概念 ; tibbit向我們展示了三項厚度的項目 , 它暗示著一個自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天行的tibbits:我們能製造出能自行製造的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 不久後 , 我們的建築物和機器將會自我組裝、複製、修復它們自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	接下來我要介紹的 , 我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後拿來和一些自然系統比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜 , 令人振奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵 , 水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶我們上太空五年的組裝時間 , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或dna有30億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎從來沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且可以修復自己延長壽命 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有種超級有趣的東西
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它轉化成我們的建築環境 , 那我們建造東西的方式就會有令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要利用我們的物理環境中的自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建設的複雜性--包括我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列--基本上是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以把該序列拿來使用 , 可以折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源將允許激活 , 讓我們的部分可以折疊程序 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的糾錯冗餘 , 以保證我們已經成功地打造我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要介紹幾個項目 , 是我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前面的兩個是macrobot和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被嵌入機電裝置、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼什麼便折疊成什麼 , 變成一連串的角度--負重120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 。 所以是一連串的角度 , 或者是輪流順序 , 你通過弦把那串序列發送出 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都需要它的消息--負120它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 參與這個計畫的設計師 ,
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想它真的能引出光線:這真的有可擴展性嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 幾千美元 , 一大堆男人為了製作這8英尺的機器人而製造 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人裝到每一個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著重被動的本質 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 嘗試以實際式計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了最基礎的計算基礎結構、數位邏輯 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nand邏輯大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 就是大門會做你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自用戶的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚塊一般 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從以前被放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會讓你在3d空間中的輸出
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要的磚塊裡插手 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它會計算它之前在做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它已經開始在三維空間中移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 它便下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它便上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著 , 我們現在的結構包含了我們所要建構的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們把所有嵌入建構的東西的信息都嵌入其中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這種情況下 , 我把它稱為自導複製 , 因為你的結構包含精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以更換零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你怎麼修理它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	因此 , 你可以擁有攀登的東西將它讀取 , 並且可以在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們目前被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它採用了可重構性和可編程性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一個元素鏈 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都是完全相同的 , 而且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一條鏈 , 或是每個元素 , 想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個情況下 , 一個螺旋 , 或者這個案例 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編寫任何立體的形狀--一維 , 二維--完全被動地進入這條鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以這告訴我們什麼關於未來的資訊 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 這告訴了我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的新可能性在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器上 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間的計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚頭都能實際計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這正是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛剛展示的這些計畫 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們能實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界做準備 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登上了月球 , 繪製了陸地圖我們甚至到達了海底最深的地點兩次 。 下一代還剩下什麼 ? 生物學家和探索者nathanwolfe提出了這個答案:幾乎所有的東西 。 然後我們開始了 , 他說 , 以一個難以置信的小世界為基礎 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	納森•沃爾夫:還有什麼好探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我是去那裡榮耀一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他當美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , andrews率領一系列到地圖上未知區域的探險活動 , 像是這裏的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是一個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他之後成為印第安納瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表公眾演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡告訴各位 , 如果有任何事情比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 它會試著要在45分鐘的演講中 , 保持一千個12歲孩童的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個問題從那時候開始就一直困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了一個問題: 「 我們應該要到哪裡去探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想 , 我們之中有很多人認為偉大的地球探索時代已經結束 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 去尋找重要的可探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有其他地方值得我們去探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想到生物學歷史中我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未見世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是取出菸草屬植物的受感染汁液 , 透過愈來愈小的過濾器過濾 ,
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他發現一定有什麼東西是比當時所知的最微小型態的生命體小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神祕經紀人命名
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之病毒--拉丁文中的 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , 實際上beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上大多數的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式生命的基因信息的總和 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實用應用和這個世界息息相關像是天花的滅絕 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 而我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現病毒
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們已經有了汽車 , 但我們還沒有意識到構成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們能夠探索未知的世界--像是深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得比只看表面還要多 , 還能觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 而是去看整個萬年紀 , 我們身邊充滿了微生物的群體 , 紀錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們能把這些技巧用在從土壤到皮膚等等所有的東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在常這樣做 , 以便找出不清楚疫情爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	先讓各位了解一下這如何運作 , 想像我們取了你們每一個人的鼻腔標本 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會找呼吸系統的病毒 , 像是流行性感冒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到一些一般的可疑物--當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分都來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到令人非常非常驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這個信息時 , 我們會發現 , 在你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息 , 與我們以前所見過的任何東西不吻合 , 不論是植物、動物、菌類、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些真的在研究這種資料的小團體 , 有幾位真的開始稱這個資訊為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是我們以前見過的任何東西 , 它就像我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達百分之四十或五十是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質 , 無法跟我們見過的任何東西歸類或配對在一起 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為或許這是人工智慧 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這信息是一種生命型態 , 至少有一部分是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	當解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都還在初步階段 , 有個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那存在於生命中 , 埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 是前所未有的生命跡象 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g當中 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命種類 , 像beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的認知 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許可以讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症病源 , 或辨識我們不熟悉的爆發病症原因 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興的宣布 , 加上史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 我們正在開始一項計畫 , 探索生物暗物質 , 以尋求新種類生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 構成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚嘆我們可能完全沒有察覺到有一種新的生命存在於我們的眼前 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的事物 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類為下一代的探險家提供了重要的課程像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們要說出這樣的一課 , 不要假設我們目前認為存在的就是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何一個你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知的事物 , 它們等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說科學家daviddeutsch將背後的理論物理物理學討論更迫切的議題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛deutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置上 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要離開肢體然後說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一件事 , 事實上 , 是歷史記錄以來大部分人都知道的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 太陽系 , 環境等等 , 都可以獨一無二地適合我們持續進化或創造 , 如同過去所想、我們現在的存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇化的名字: 「 地球號太空船 」 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	太空船之外的宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 而它的內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們所依賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	只有一次機會:如果我們把太空船搞亂 , 就沒有其他地方可以去了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都已經知道的事和人類歷史大部份時候所相信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如同史蒂芬霍金說過的 , 我們只是在一個典型的星球表面的化學汙垢 , 環繞著一個典型的恆星 , 它就在一個典型的星系的最外圍 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道兩件事中的第一件事有點像是在說我們正處於一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合之類的第二件事則是說我們正處於一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你把這兩項當作深奧的真理來生存 , 以及告訴你的人生決策 , 那麼他們似乎彼此會有一點點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩人完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二點開始:典型的 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們看看四周 , 往一個隨機的方向看 , 我們看到一面牆 , 和化學污垢 , 這些都不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝著同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看見任何牆壁或化學汙垢 , 你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 太陽系 , 星星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這在宇宙中仍然不算典型 。 因為恆星存在於星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部份地方 , 宇宙中典型的地方 , 都離任何星系都還差得遠 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 再進一步 , 直到我們走出星系 , 再往回看 , 沒錯 , 星系有著巨大的螺旋臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	到這個時候 , 我們已經有十萬光年的光年
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們離宇宙中一個典型的地方還很近 ,
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須跨銀河間的空間 , 千倍以上才能到達 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在極大的開銷上 , ted針對內部空間排列了高清晰的虛擬實境視角--星系間空間的景觀.
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 這樣我們看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	呃 , 還不完全完美你可以看到在星系間的空間裡是完全黑暗 , 一片漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你離你最近的恆星看向你 , 那顆恆星就是在爆炸 , 身為超新星的你 , 當光線射到你的時候 , 你仍然無法看到甚至閃閃閃發亮的光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	那就是宇宙有多大、多麼暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管如此 , 一顆超新星就這麼明亮 , 這麼傑出的一個事件 , 它會在數光年的範圍內把你石頭殺死 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你根本不會看見它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷 , 溫度不到絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它非常的空洞 。 真空吸塵器的密度 , 比我們目前所能創造出的最高真空還要小一百萬倍 。 這就是典型的地方 , 離這個地方有多不一樣 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	那就是這地方是如此地不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 請把燈光再打回來 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何得知一個離我們如此遙遠的環境 , 如此不同外星人 , 從我們習慣的事物 , 知道了嗎 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	那麼 , 地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這代表什麼呢 ? 看看比我們更遠--我是指從這裡以望遠鏡看 , 你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 類星體 」 。 類星體原意是指類星體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像恆星的東西 。 但又不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 幾十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量黑洞塌陷.
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用.其中一些物質 , 以極大的噴射流形式回到外面 , 以光滑的形式照亮了葉片 , 我認為它有著數兆個太陽的光亮.
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人腦的物理學很難不像這種噴射流的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不可能一瞬間存活下來 。 當語言試圖描述這些噴射流中的情況時 , 我們無法一瞬間存活下來 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	那會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在零距離及數百萬年 , 每次都是如此 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生得如此精確 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你有參考正在發生的 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個同類的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是膚淺的圖像 , 雖然也包含這樣的圖像 , 還有解釋性的模型 , 呈現出相同的數學關係和因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠奇妙 , 信心和另一種結構相似會隨著時間而增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這樣特別的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 儘可能不像它們彼此相似 , 儘管它們能以相同的數學和因果結構體現出相同的數學和因果結構 , 且會隨著時間而不斷地重複上演 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	我們的化學污垢是不同的 , 這種化學污垢有著普遍的通性
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構精密度不斷提高 , 無所不在的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙的其它地方 , 是一個由內而外包含構成的樞紐 。 整個實體的結構和因果的精髓 。 如此一來 , 物理定律不會允許這一切發生 , 或者甚至強調這可能是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 與宇宙的其他部分 , 如何形成這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 它是對的 , 但它是錯的--強調是錯的 。 有一點是錯的 , 它不使用任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它用三樣我們這裡有豐富的事物就可以做到 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是運算的 , 計算需要電腦是無所不在的製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的 , 使得媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	接著 , 第三點 , 比較不容易體會 , 但就如同 , 公開創造知識、解釋的必要性一樣 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	譬如說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律在300年前進行測試
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 過去我們所做的證據 , 早在那之前的數十億年 , 就在地球上的每一平方公尺都掉落了 , 之後的數十億年 , 還會繼續下去 。 對其他的科學也一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學中最基本的真理的證據就在我們星球上的真理 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地充滿了證據 , 同時也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件在其最低的可能性上 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 暗在那裡 , 還是那裡 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 那只是另一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像在星系間空間中的一個立方體 , 就跟我們的家一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 這個立方體非常空 , 用人類的標準來看 , 但這仍然意味著 , 它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠建造一個自給自足的太空站 , 其中有一群科學家 , 他們致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類的 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技已經遠遠超越了從星系間空間收集氫氣再將其轉化成其他的元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但重點是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某物不被物理定律所禁止 , 那還有什麼能讓我們不去做 , 除了知道如何做以外呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到那我們就會自動獲得能源供應 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣的 , 對人類的感官來說那裡也是黑暗的 。 但你所要做的是拿個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的一個設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到同樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	透過更強大的望遠鏡你將可以看到恆星和行星
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律.
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡你可以打造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能就是生物學實地考察 , 因為要到達最近的有生命得星球 , 得花上數億年的時間 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但我從來都不太喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年才做一次.
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了開放式知識創造的所有前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都有可能變成和我們一樣的中心 , 只要我們知道該怎麼做就在那裡 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不在一個獨特的適合人居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解釋方式 , 那幾乎所有其他的環境也是一樣的 。 地球的污染程度也是一樣 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而知識 , 非常缺乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個知識型的宇宙觀也許──我認為應該要讓我們覺得很特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為如果沒有那些必要的具體的知識 , 我們就無法生存 , 無法生存 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星 , 幾光年外就會熄滅 , 我們都將會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 還有對大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義更是如此 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機率能存活在這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在研討會上談到
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為這種機率是適當的 , 可以用來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們能生存 , 我們不能生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險性不是空前的 , 物種隨時會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明的結局 。 絕大多數的物種以及所有曾經存在過的文明 , 都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來說 , 我們唯一的希望是利用區分我們物種的這個特徵 , 和我們的文明 , 和其他所有這些特徵中 , 即我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋、新的知識的能力 , 成為存在的中心 。
