so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 現在讓我把它用在當前的一個爭議上 , 並不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所說的這類的爭議 。
and the controversy is global warming .	這場爭論是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種正確的物理學家 。 考慮到全球暖化 , 我只是一個懶人 。 要讓一個懶惰 , 理性的做法 , 就是認真看待現有的科學理論 。 而根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避開災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果目前我們最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費數千億美元的龐大成本 , 那麼不論如何是好 , 那都已經是個災難了 , 不論是任何合理的措施了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行動甚至都沒有被提出來解決問題 , 只是稍微延後一些而已 。 所以這已經太遲了 , 而且可能已經太遲了 , 在任何人意識到這個危險之前 , 都無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河期 , 數十億人將會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有告知公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法一直知道 。 當我們知道有一場即將到來的災難的發生 , 以及如何以不如災難本身的成本來解決它 , 那麼真的就不會有太多爭論說了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 而不只是問題解決 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒方法但只有在我們知道預防什麼的情況下
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學就不是教你如何避免拳頭被打 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 只專注在預防 , 那麼它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在用計劃來強行減少氣體排放 , 不計成本 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計劃一樣 , 以減少溫度計 , 並計劃在更高的環境中生活 , 不計成本 , 只需使用高溫 , 便宜又便宜 。 此類計劃的確存在 。 例如 , 空間中有成群的鏡頭來將陽光往外移 , 並鼓勵水生生物去吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 或大體上的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒有意識到的問題 , 有能力去做正確的事──不是無限期的幸運──是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 更是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩塊石板在上面刻上
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	在其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 "
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果被困在一個不好的體制下 , 國家要如何擺脫貧困呢 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默開啟了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區市政府 」 , 「 城市管理區 」 , 由各國聯盟所統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的激進想法: 「 特區市 」
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	對我們來說 , 它是一個非常引人入勝的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做功課在首都機場的路燈下因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我也見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	讓我們選一張來舉例 , 綠色襯衣的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們來給他個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森擁有手機
so here is the puzzle .	所以這個謎題是
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以取得像手機那樣尖端的科技產品 , 卻無法取得一百年的科技來提供家裡的電燈用品呢 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的制度 , 可以防止雙贏解決方案的產生 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人也能使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循的規則運作 , 也就是說 , 它必須以非常低廉的補貼價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 這個價格低到它每賣出的單位 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既不具有資源 , 也不具激勵機制 , 可以吸引許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 是有可能有不同的規則 , 企業可以賺取小額利潤 , 所以他們有動機去登記更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	正是尼爾森電信公司通過在電信公司從基礎下操作他的電話時所採用的規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經知道這些規則如何好好運作了 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電來定價的規則 , 但卻跑到企業和消費者的抗議當中 , 他們想要保存既有補貼的比例 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他深陷其中一些規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson則卡在路燈下讀書
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能制定一些規則來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我主張 , 有一種抽象的洞見我們可以做實際的做法 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人民更多的選擇 , 和更多的領導者更多的選擇 , 在許多國家 , 也都是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現出這兩者間的反對聲浪很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導人的那種選擇 , 像給總統選擇提高電價的選擇 , 奪走經濟裡人們所想要的這個選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一方或另一方 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那會給我們一組規則 , 用來改變規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則所造成的破壞 , 規則能讓大家留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間的地球照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你把這裡放大 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這條線外 , 跟鄰近黑洞相比 , 它就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現 , 北韓的體制使人留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是要了解北韓和南韓開始時用的是一模一樣的規則 , 不論是法律或法規 , 都一樣 , 但在更深層的理解力、標準、文化、價值觀、信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 導致他們形成一組規則 , 非常多樣化的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們能改變──我們人類能改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡是一條線 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗與它的鄰居多明尼加相比 , 那裡的居民人數也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各 , 他們的居民數目只有海地或多明尼加共和國的一半 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是體制之所以不良 , 是因為政府的軟弱
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	這不僅僅是規則不好 , 因為政府過於強勢和壓迫 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造一個有良好體制的環境 , 我們不能僅僅撕下去 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法去建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地證明了與規則一起工作的潛在和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料圖表的一開始 , 中國是高科技領導者 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人的科技像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等都是先驅
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 以有效的制度來鼓勵這些想法的傳播一個有利潤的動機 , 來鼓勵這些想法的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用規則來放慢創新並切斷中國和世界其他地方的關係 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以當其他國家在創新 , 以發展更新的科技 , 同時發展更新的規則 , 中國也被切斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入高於世界其他地方的收入都停滯不前
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製的是中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代時你可以看到這個數字大約在3%左右 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況有了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國開始起飛中國人開始很快地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到夜晚的地圖 , 你可以找到引起中國規則劇烈變化的線索 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的這個點 , 大家可以在輪廓邊緣看到 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都是遵循一套截然不同的規則 , 與當時中國大陸其他地方的法則相比 , 當時中國的市場經濟制度早已實施 , 而且由英國人負責 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在50年代 , 香港是一個數百萬人都可以去的地方 , 從大陸到成家 , 像是縫紉上衣、製作玩具等工作 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但是 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 在那裡成長迅速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本 , 像鄧小平這種領導者能夠複製 , 當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有人立刻轉向市場模式 , 不如說設立一些特區去做些什麼 , 某種意義上是英國人所做的:讓機會與市場規則去合作 , 讓那些想參與的人們一起合作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建了四個經濟特區:讓中國人能夠前往工作區 , 都市很快地成長 ; 也有區域 , 外國企業可以進來生產 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個特區 , 有一座城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市有台灣企業 , 讓在座很多人都擁有iphone , 且他們是由中國人搬到深圳去的中國勞工 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿海城市 , 在相同的意義下 , 最終 , 在這些地方人民可以選擇成功 , 他們聚集起來 , 因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	成功的實現後 , 促成了大家對於整個經濟體的市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了以下幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	一是保留給人們的選擇
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模是對的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的體制 , 你可以這麼做 , 但一個村莊會太小 , 以至於無法得到你所能得到的益處 , 如果你有數百萬人 , 所有人都遵守好的體制 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家的規模太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試圖改變國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他的人先放大再嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你這個機會 , 來創造新地方 , 用新規則 , 讓大家可以選擇選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們的規模足夠大 , 足以讓我們在數百萬人共同合作時 , 獲得所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以這個提議就是我們構思了一個叫做 " 特區市 " 的東西
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個明確規範的憲章開始 , 來吸引那些需要我們建設城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引那些會建立起基礎設施的投資者──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引企業他們會先請來搬移的人
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	然後你會需要吸引家家戶戶願意搬來住 , 永久居住在那裡 , 養育子女 , 為子女接受教育 , 得到第一份工作
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那章節 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	這座城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以把這個模型的規模做大 ,
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些被大眾捕捉到的憲章
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這才是真正建構在這個模型上 , 如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從無人之地開始 ,
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以進到新的憲章之下去住 , 但沒有人被迫在此之下去住 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的領導者們的選擇我們必須允許國家之間互相合作的可能性 。 實際上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先是市場模式的奴隸 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 透過在香港的行動 , 不經意地減少了世界的貧窮現象 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫的數目還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們能讓這些合作關係再度重現 , 我們就能讓全世界都受惠 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	某些情況下 , 這會牽扯到負責任的地位 , 將控制權從一個國家帶到另一個國家 , 來擔起某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始會想: 「 這只會讓殖民主義回來嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但很重要的是要體認到當我們開始思考這些事情時會產生的那種情緒 , 會阻礙我們拉扯 , 會讓我們停止、關閉自己的能力 , 以及探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在一些援助計畫中 , 殘留的不良是 , 它涉及了強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式的重點在於選擇 , 無論是領袖 , 還是那些將生活在這些新地方的人民 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是消除強制力和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	讓我們來談談如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們選個特別的領導人 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的 , 但他在古巴並沒有一個香港就在古巴的島嶼上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他還是有一點點光線在南部 , 那裡有著很特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在美國的行政條約為一塊大概是曼哈頓的兩倍大的土地 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理說: 「 聽著 , 洋基斯有個可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你 , 加拿大 , 為何不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建設一個特殊的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新的城市在那上面興建 ,
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來 ,
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那座城市 ,
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會擋住 , 但這將會是把現代經濟和現代世界連結到我的國家的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模式還可以在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我已經和非洲的領導人談過了 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們中的許多人完全了解一個特區的想法 , 讓大家可以選擇作為一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這種制度的改變規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種制定新規則的方式 , 人們不需要強迫 , 也不需要強制 , 迫使強制的反對者也能強制執行 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全理解在某些情況下他們可以對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾這些投資者將會建造港口 , 建設港口 , 建造道路 , 在新城市裡 , 他們可以做出更有保障的承諾只要他們能與合夥的國家一起做 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	或許甚至在某些安排有點像信託管理帳戶 , 你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 合作國家要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是一張我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地有數億人可以居住
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們總結一下 , 不只想著一個或兩個特區的城市 , 而是數十個將會幫助創造數億人居住城市的城市 , 可能是數十億人 , 在未來的世紀會搬移到城市去 , 那裡有足夠的土地供他們使用 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們晚上看這些燈光 , 有一件事是誤導人的 , 就是看起來世界上大部分的地區都已經被建立起來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我來說明為何這樣做是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把所有土地的呈現方式
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經佔據了三十億人居住的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現這些有30億城市的城市只佔了地球上所有可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想要為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們就會變成這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從可耕地的3%走到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大減少人類在地球上的足跡 , 做法是建立更多人類能搬移的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是依照好的規則來管理 , 它們可以是安全的城市 , 在城市中 , 人們被犯罪、疾病 , 以及不良的公共衛生 , 這些城市是有機會找到工作的 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	能取得像電力這樣的基礎公共事業
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 建立 「 特區 」 城市 , 要花什麼代價 ? 要打造出第一座 「 特區 」 城市 , 才能做得更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	才能有一本手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的就是撰寫一些細節 , 可能進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理這些城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們胡思亂想 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考像這樣的問題 , 假設不只加拿大和卡斯楚之間有關係 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參加了 , 西班牙也一樣 。 或許古巴想成為四向合作企業的一員 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有先例可循 , 但很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們該如何資助 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港都是城市 , 為他們剛起步時所擁有的土地 , 創造了巨大的價值 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地價值的收益來支付像警察 , 法庭費用但是學校系統 , 和健康照護系統 , 也讓這塊地更吸引人生活 , 使得人們有高收入的地區 , 順便一提 , 使土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建設這個區域的人的獎勵 , 並且建立起基本的規則 , 大致上是正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其它的細節 , 像這樣 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓那些在第一份工作就很便宜、負擔得起的建築 , 把類似iphone的建築物組裝起來 , 讓那些建築物能更有效率 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下去 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節尚待解決 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 早就知道 , 沒有路上的阻礙 , 沒有阻礙 , 除了我們缺乏想像力之外 , 還會讓我們無法真正地提供真正的全球性雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們能過得好的原因 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們就和我們分享了 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀有物品 , 分享代表我們每個人都會獲取較少的 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式來思考想法 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:制度主宰我們彼此的互動規則例如 , 讓我們來訂個賦稅制度支撐一個研究大學提供一些免費的知識
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有個制度 , 在這個制度中 , 我們擁有一塊土地 , 用政府的辦公室來註冊 , 讓大家可以宣誓為附屬品做準備 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在制度上創新 , 尤其是為了改變制度而想出一些規則的創新 , 那麼我們就不會卡在不良的制度上 , 那麼我們就能不斷進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 這樣尼爾森和他的朋友就不再需要在路燈下學習了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特從他史詩般的圓環世界遠征起 , 談到他的團隊目前為止發現的數百萬個基因 , 用來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	craigventer在dna和海洋上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	在休息的時候 , 我被幾個人問到關於我對於老化的辯論
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將會是我對它唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者非常過於生存的悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在這18分鐘裡我將告訴你們的是我們如何從破解基因密碼轉換到開始自我編碼的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前的這個月當我們公佈了第一組取自一種非寄生有機體的基因序列叫做嗜血桿菌
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月進行基因組研究 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八小時來完成相同的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加進來了:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前這個階段的基因組學研究發現 , 到今年年年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的測序 , 大概是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得贊助 , 到今年進行130組基因組的測序 , 作為一個來自環境有機體的副方案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因編碼的速度改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 我們看看 , 外面到底有什麼 , 我們幾乎不在地球上現有的東西上劃分出表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都沒有意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球上生物總量的一半 。 而所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	可能是牛津人很常做的事 , 但如果你曾經到過海裡 , 吞一口海水 , 別忘了 , 每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前的特徵 , 不到五千種微生物種類 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了第二次足球探險 , 在那裡 , 進行了很棒的海洋考察 , 嘗試每200英哩進行一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 到美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱辛的任務 ; 我們在帆船上這樣做 , 有部分是要協助讓年輕人興奮地進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗是非常簡單的
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要把海水過濾掉 , 用不同的濾器收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回在岩城的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以每24小時完成一億個字母的基因編碼排序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這個活動 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 一般認為在我們眼裡的視覺色素只有一兩種有機體具有相同色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎全世界上半部海域的所有物種 , 都有著相同的感光受體 , 利用陽光作為牠們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新的基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在將它延伸至空氣中 , 加上史隆基金會的贊助 ,
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌全部人每天都呼出 , 特別是在飛機上或是密閉的講堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們利用一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 僅僅一天之內我們在紐約市的一棟大樓上蒐集到10億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在進行這些測序的過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	光是在收集資料方面 , 就在加拉巴哥群島的位置上 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每隔200英哩 , 我們在海洋中可以看到非常多樣的樣本 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是有邏輯的 , 就不同溫度的梯度而言 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的--我們發現 , 溫水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 , 很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一個令我們相當驚訝的是這些感光細胞會感應不同波長的光線 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測這個現象 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	從地區到地區的這些差異極大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 感光細胞傾向於看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化會更大 , 可能會更趨向紅外線和紫外線 , 在極端的狀況下 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們基因庫的樣子 , 我們整合了所有資料 , 包括所有遠離探索的資料 , 這些資料代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總計大約有2千9百萬組基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家族裡 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但是我們在環境中採取的每個新樣本都加入了這些新族群的線性樣本 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於發現基礎基因、元件與生命的最初階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看那些所謂的 「 演化樹 」 , 我們就站在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	大約2千9百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有2萬4千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物的基因放在一起 , 我們所共有的基因族群大概只有三萬不到一個 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為 , 現在這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為以基因為中心 , 也許可以回溯到理查•達金斯的想法而不是基因組中心論 , 而是這些基因組成的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力 , 合成dna的能力在過去十年到二十年間都大大改變了dna定序的速度 , 且越來越快又便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對於人造基因組的第一個想法來自於1995年我們在第二組基因組的測序出現 , 而這起源於mycoplasma生殖支原體 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有非常棒的t恤衫上面說: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們單純地問一個問題:如果一個物種需要八百種 , 另外五百種 , 有比較小的基因組 , 可能會組成一個最小的作業系統嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨意放入基因編碼的小段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因中間 , 就會打斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有所有能接受轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境對此是非常重要的 , 你只能依據周遭環境的本質來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智力方法來研究13種相似有機物的基因組 , 我們試著去比較所有這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	然後我們有了這些重疊的圓形 。 然後我們發現 , 在這13種有機體中 , 只有173個基因都很常見 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池子如果我們忽略了一個細胞內的寄生蟲 , 會稍微擴大一些 , 當我們觀察核心基因組時 , 大約310組左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	因此我們認為可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 取決於你在這裡的觀點 , 或許300到400個基因 , 來自最少500個 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一可以證明這些想法的方法是建造一個人造的染色體 , 裡面有那些基因 , 我們不得不以模組式的方式來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現大片碎片中合成精確的dna實在是非常困難
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 同時也是我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法能讓我們在兩週內合成出5000個鹼基對的病毒在基因序列與生物學上的精確度達到100%的精確率
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這個實驗非常令人興奮 , 當時我們將合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始促成病毒粒子的製造 , 轉過來殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是人造病毒的第一年發明小兒麻痺病毒但只有原先的十分之一活躍用了三年的時間
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是 , 軟體現在打造自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	大家馬上跳到關心生物戰的議題上 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 也是美國政府設立的專門委員會來檢討這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為將現實記在心中是很重要的 , 與人們想像力的後果 , 兩者是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成測序的病毒基因組都可以
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會馬上對伊波拉病毒或天花的事件感到驚恐 , 但這個有機體的dna並沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造出天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的 , 是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國 , 做了許多努力 , 致力於創造生物戰的媒介 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被終止了 , 那將來在製造設計病毒上就應該不會有太多的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞有機體就有可能成真 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	那些我們已經擁有的真核細胞 , 可能在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變放入這個人造染色體的卡帶和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把所有其他的部分都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組的重組系統 , 將這些片段組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體得來的deinoccusradiodurans得來的它可以承受三百萬雷得的輻射而且不會被殺死
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後它會在12至24小時內重組自己的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 也許現在的外太空是因為我們在那裡的所有旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過50萬拉德輻射照射過後的杯子 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始碎裂 , 微生物停留在底部 , 變得更開心也更開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是實際情況的照片上面的圖片顯示經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的會被炸開 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是相同的dna在24小時後自行重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些生物能做到這一點 , 真的很讓人吃驚 , 我們可能有數千種 , 甚至數以萬計地球上有不同種類的生物 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此我們認為人造細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 同時也是希望具有環境和社會議題的基礎 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上詹氏甲烷鏈球菌──它生存在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它所獲得的碳元素來自環境 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 現在有數千種不同的生物 , 它們都從二氧化碳中生存下來 , 還能追溯回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	因此 , 與其使用從石油中取得的碳來進行製程 , 我們有機會使用碳並將它從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 能在一氧化碳中生存 , 我們把水分解成可以產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有數條路徑可以改造甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦公司在挪威石油公司有個大型專案 , 專門從天然氣場取得並將那裡的甲烷轉變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的一刻 , 我認為會有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些巨大的基因陣列和同源重組方法 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 讓機器人每天製造出也許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學一樣 , 你可以通過篩選來獲得選擇 , 無論是用來篩選氫氣製成或是化學製成 , 還是僅限於可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若想了解這些基因在一定程度上扮演的角色
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用的過程 , 直接從陽光產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為這個過程會完全改變 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 將複雜糖分解的酶 , 將糖分解成簡單糖類 , 在同一個細胞中發酵 , 以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	利用微生物進行製藥生產的研究已經在主要實驗室中進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	來自環境中的化合物的化學成分 , 比我們最佳化學家所能產出的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許可以取代整個石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 ,
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	那其實是個非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都在用他們的教義作為法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何在禁止製造生命的條件 , 所以這方面一定是沒問題的 。 最終的顧慮才是生物戰的方面 , 卻給了我們開始進行這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛剛資助了一個多機構的研究項目來探究這個項目對社會的風險和益處也就是科學團隊如我自己的團隊所應該在這個領域使用的規則我們試著在未來建立好的例子
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 可以讓我們設計來產生乾淨能源 , 也許可以徹底改變發展中國家可以做到的 , 並提供各種簡單的處理 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利浦津巴多說 , 快樂和成功都根植在我們大多數人不重視的特質中:我們以朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議 , 我們準時校準自己的觀點 , 以改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一間健康的手段 , 就在時間上 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些想法 , 關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始時鐘--拜託 。 三十秒 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	這是關於時間 , 結束序列 。 拿一個吧 。

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來聽聽亞當的誘惑對談 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當上來吧 , 別那麼渴望洗腦 。 吃一口吧 。 」 「 我照做了 。 」

" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 咬一口 。 到底在幹嘛 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生就是誘惑 。 這一切都是為了產出 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 此時此刻 , 衝動 , 衝動性 , 集中精神 , 現在和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會落入當下的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚姻前承諾要保持貞操的少女感謝小布施-大多數 , 約有60% , 會在一年內違背性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	而且大多都不使用避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	非常適合做承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在來試試四歲的小孩 , 讓他們接受治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但是如果他們在等待實驗員回來 , 他們就可以擁有兩顆了 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 這要付出代價 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 要等 ,
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的事是三分之二的孩子們給予誘惑
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等.其他人當然會等了.
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 他們延遲到來
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我斯坦福大學的同事 , 在14年後 , 試著去發現那些孩子不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 反抗的孩子和產生出來的孩子有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	在sat考試中 , 抗拒得分超過250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 , 就像是一整組不同的iq點
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們並沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們有自信和堅定的決心 。 而我今天的關鍵 , 你們的關鍵在於 , 他們的未來會被焦點放在而非現在的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 如何將你的人類經歷的流動分成時間區域或時間範疇 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動地、無意識地去做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平都不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了過度使用它們 , 其他的基礎設施也會不被使用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出的決策是基於動作 ,
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 這只是關於當下情況 , 別人做些什麼 , 及你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以這種形式做決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀導向 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在的狀況 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不重要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	重點是 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況如何 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們就把這些人稱之為 " 懷舊之輩 " 因為他們關注的重點
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是和預期結果有關 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱他們為 「 未來式 」 。 他們關注的重點在於將來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我要提出一個論點 , 時間觀念的悖論 , 是影響你做的每個決策 , 你完全沒有意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 從這些偏見的角度來看的話
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以當下 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以 「 懷舊 」 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你也可以稱它為人性主義 , 即你專注於生活的歡樂 , 或是當今的財富主義者--這無關緊要 , 你的生活受到控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 「 未來 」 、 「 設定目標 」 ,
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命始於死亡之後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 轉移時間觀點的流暢度 , 取決於對局勢的需求 , 這是你學會的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度 " 未來
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代社會主義的溫和 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	並且總是低於負面及時髦 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最佳時光色的混合 , 就是你從過去得到的積極樂觀 , 給你根源 。 你連結你的家庭、身份、以及你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來你能得到的是一對翅膀 , 可以飛到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現今的享樂主義得到的能量、能量 , 來探索自己、地點、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光裡的負面比正面的還多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間 ; 犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 ; 犧牲個人崇拜時光 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠.這會影響他們的健康.
and they live for work , achievement and control .	為工作、成就與控制權而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted會員共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這句話引起我的共鳴 。 我從小在南布朗克斯貧民窟長大 , 一個西西里島的家庭 , 每個人過去和現在都生活在過去 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡 , 身為一個未來的前輩 , 走到頂端 , 做出這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了 , 使我成為有前途的人 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果等一下 , 你會得到兩顆棉花糖 , 直到我學會保持平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入現今的社會人士主義 , 把焦點放在過時的積極 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個方法用在許多世界性問題上:改變輟學率 , 讓學童們上癮、更強化青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻法來治療退伍軍人的創傷 , 例如 , 奇蹟般的治癒人 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體康復費用 , 此項目有50%的退出率 , 改變有自殺式恐怖分子的訴求 , 修正家庭關係 , 修正長期進行的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 我想說的是:生活中的許多謎題都可以解決 , 透過了解你的時間觀及其他人的時間觀 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	當今的頭條中有多少人會在100年後才會重要呢 ? 1000年 ? 柯克.卡特朗的 「 長遠新聞 」 計畫收集當今不只如此 , 還會在幾十年後引起共鳴 , 在ted2010年 , 他針對近期頭條發出 「 有可能型塑我們未來 」 的標題 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題 , 媒體 , 新聞 , 科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是 ,
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 那些故事有多少意義 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞的概念 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是由tedsters所創立的 " 長遠的基金會 " 計畫包括kevinkelly和stewartbrand
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們在尋找的可能是50或100或100 , 000年後仍然存在的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你看新聞 , 通過過濾器 , 很多會掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿去年a.p.的頂尖故事來說 , 十年後還會有影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會造成影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 聽起來很酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟問題 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這次經濟衰退 , 就會變成陳年往事 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事會對未來造成影響 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就科學而言 ,
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	總有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液流動 , 修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 某天就已經在這了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真的蜜蜂毒液攻擊腫瘤 ; 牠們把基因送到大腦中 ; 牠們建造的機器人可以在人體中爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們餵養六十億人是有困難的 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 這裡有超過10億人正處於飢餓狀態 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	沒有經過基因改造作物 , 英國人會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲在農業研究上已經賭上了十億 。
what about global politics ?	那麼國際政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會有很大的不同 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 而且他們可以 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始在兒童身上做dna檢測 , 來選擇職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種途徑 , 將我們所知道的部份向後推進 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	近期有了新的發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有自導的機器人 , 已經有科學家很快地發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能不再需要我們 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年之後就在清醒過來了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎有沒有我們 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 去年 , 我選了長期新聞長篇大論 , 就是這則新聞:在月球上發現了水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要想把一個蟻群放上去就容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫下大筆的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco則顯示從卡西尼航行到土星的照片 , 關注的是它的最大衛星:泰坦 , 和結冰的土衛二上 , 這似乎對冰噴射機造成了衝擊 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	太空總署 , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco要我們飛往土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會帶大家去一趟旅程 ,
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程是你和我多年來的至今展開 , 大約五十年前 , 當人類第一次離開地球時 , 這趟旅程便開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅真的踏上了月球的實體 , 我們還把飛行器發送給了所有的八個行星 , 我們已經在小行星上著陸 , 和彗星相連 , 到這一刻 , 我們有一架太空飛船正往冥王星的路上 , 前身為行星的行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟用來了解某樣東西的旅程 , 來感知我們的宇宙地點 , 了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的星球 , 我們的星球 , 以及我們賴以生存的星球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在所有太陽系中我們可以去尋找這樣的問題的所在地 , 這裡有土星 。 我們在1980年代早期造訪過土星之前就已經到過土星了 。 但是我們對土星的調查自從卡西尼號太空船開始進行了更加深入的探究 , 經過了7年行星間的太空飛行 , 在2004年夏天穿越土星運行軌道後 , 發現了當時人類抵達土星的最遠的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它帶來了神秘 , 科學的洞察力 , 顯然遠超出了比較 , 這系統的研究 , 具有巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就很清楚知道了很多關於恆星和氣體的光碟 。 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張仙女星雲的優美照片 , 是我們離銀河系最近 , 最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這是由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝的旋渦星系 , 美麗的複合體 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 返回土星的這段旅程 , 其實是人類旅程的一部分 , 也是用來做大一點的比喻 , 用來了解我們身邊所有事物之間的聯繫 , 以及人類要如何融入這片土星 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法用卡西尼號的作品來告訴各位我們所學的所有東西 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們過去兩年半拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我實在的時間不夠 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把焦點放在最令人興奮的故事中 , 從這次大型探索探索土星探險旅程中出來的兩則是最令人興奮的 , 且已經在過去兩年半了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	陪伴在土星上的是一系列非常大又多樣的衛星大集合 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸從幾公里寬延伸到全美大的範圍 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝到土星的美麗圖片事實上陪伴著土星的月球 。 這是土星和土星的土衛二 , 這是土星的地形 , 這裡是土星的地形邊緣 , 向你展示他們有多麼地薄 , 有著月亮的土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中有2顆是站立著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二恩克拉多斯 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的單獨地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	長久以來 , 看著行星的人都感到興趣 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為是跟我們在地球上的環境一樣 , 至少在過去 , 比起其它在太陽系中的天體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中大致上就是氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣層中含有簡單的有機物質 , 像是甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六的大氣中被分解 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造出霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物無所不在 , 完全被全球化的土衛六包圍 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你無法用我們的眼睛看向水面 , 在可見的光譜區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但是這些霧狀顆粒 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 經過了數十億年的變化 , 溫和的飄移到水面上 , 將表面覆蓋在厚有機泥土中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以像泰坦相當於焦油 , 油 , 或什麼我們不知道 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在土衛六的地表溫度下可以是液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是土衛六的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是會冷凝的 , 所以 , 承認這種情況 , 就會帶到世界各地的奇特可能性 。 你可以有甲烷做的雲 , 在那些雲之上 , 像這樣的霧狀雲 , 可以防止陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度大約是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管溫度很低 , 土衛六表面可能會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨水在地球上做什麼:它會雕刻水溝 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中結合 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它能把泥狀物從高山和山丘上沖下來 , 進入低地 。 所以停下來想一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的地表會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它黑暗 。 土衛六上的中午和地球上深處的暮光同樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 很陰森 , 很惡劣 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在上面塗料稀釋劑的密西根湖邊 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達之前的土衛六地表的景象 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 雖然這和那個故事並不相同 , 但它卻非常精彩 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 它就像卡西尼號的人--它一直就像是朱爾凡爾納的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說的 , 它有很厚的層次大氣 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 太陽的背光 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	那裡還有一隻衛星--我不知道是哪一顆 。 這是一顆很大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 可以透過這個大氣層看到水面 , 我的照相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍攝了像這樣的照片
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是又亮又暗的區域 , 那大約是對我們而言的程度 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法知道我們在土衛六上看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你看得更仔細一點 , 你就會開始看到像我們不知道的無數通道 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 這實際上是一個隕石坑 , 但是在土衛六的表面 , 只有少數隕石坑 , 意即這是一個非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有一些構造的特徵看起來
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來像是被拉開了
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上的任何線性 , 代表有一個斷層 , 像一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以已經在地質上有了改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入環地軌道六個月後 , 一件事情發生了 , 許多人視為卡西尼號突出的泰坦星影像 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 。 歐洲建造的惠更斯基探測器載運了七年穿過太陽系 。 我們將它佈署到土衛六的大氣中 , 花了兩個半小時 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想要強調這事件的重要性 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的儀器 , 它第一次在外太陽系的天體落入人類歷史上 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心目中 , 這件事意義重大 , 以至於在我腦海中 , 這個活動本來應該是和滴答的遊行一起舉行 , 遍及美國和歐洲各個城市 , 很遺憾 , 事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是國際間的使命 。 這個活動在歐洲、德國被舉行 , 慶祝會上有英國口音 , 還有美國口音 , 還有德國口音 , 法國人、義大利人、和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個關於 「 聯合國 」 應有的動作展示了真國聯合一同努力做出好事
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是一個需要探索行星的龐大任務 , 為了要了解一個行星系統 , 在整個人類歷史上 , 它是不可預測的 , 現在 , 人類真的接觸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以這--我是說 , 光是說 , 就起雞皮疙瘩了 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一場極度激動人心的事件 , 而這也是我個人永遠無法忘記的事 , 你也不應如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在下降的途中對大氣進行了測量 , 它也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法用言語來告訴你們第一次看到土衛六地表照片是什麼感覺 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	很讓人震驚 , 因為這是我們希望其他由軌道拍攝的照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是獨一無二的模式 , 地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種樹枝滴水的圖案 , 只靠液體的流動才能形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道走 , 可以看到它們的匯合方式 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯聚到這裡的這個通道 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你們現在看到的是一條海岸線 ,
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這卻是一條海岸線
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里的高度拍攝的 ,
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里高拍攝的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好了 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是一個航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機穿越美國 , 你會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在鐵達尼亞航空窗上 , 飛越土衛六時的照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器停留在地表上 , 我要給各位看看 , 各位女士、先生們 , 這是在外太陽系的一個月球表面前所拍攝的第一張照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些水可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對吧 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯 , 它落在了其中一塊平坦的陰影地帶 。 它沒有沉沒消失 。 所以它不是我們降落在黑暗地帶的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器下來的基本上等同於一塊泥漿 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個沒有被分解的土地 , 裡面充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很可能 , 這種材料已經用我們看到的這些管道沖洗掉土衛六上的高地 , 流過數十億年來累積在低窪的盆地上 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 仍然沒有任何跡象在我們的影像中 , 或甚至是惠更斯的影像中 , 存在著任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們到哪裡去了 ? 發現沙丘時 , 更令人費解 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道附近的電影 , 展示了這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高 , 被幾公里高的沙丘分隔著 , 綿延了幾英哩 , 綿延了幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有幾百英里 , 高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很明顯地 , 這個地方非常乾燥 , 否則不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以又一次的 , 困惑到沒有體液的存在 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	還有土衛六南極的一個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	差不多跟安大略湖一樣大
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	後來 , 僅僅一個禮拜半前 , 我們飛過了土衛六的北極 , 發現了相當於加斯波尼亞海域的大小 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 基於某些原因 , 我們不了解液體 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 土衛六的兩極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個不可思議的地方 。 它是異國的 , 它是異國的 , 但又和地球有著奇特的相似處 。 它有著像地球表面的地質構造及極大的地質多樣性 。 它是一個迷人的世界 , 在太陽系中 , 複雜而豐富的環境中 , 只有地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們來看看土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小型衛星 , 大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在旁邊 , 只是爲了向你展示它的尺寸 。 這並不是一個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二非常白 , 非常明亮 , 它的表面顯然有裂痕 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的發現 , 發現地點是在南極 , 我們看到這裡的南極 , 在那裡 , 我們發現了這個裂痕系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同是因為它們的組成不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些裂痕覆蓋著有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地區的溫度也提升了 。 這裡是整個星球溫度最高的地方 , 在身體上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就好像發現地球上的南極洲比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 我們拍攝了額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些地裂中 , 會噴射出細小的冰粒 , 噴射範圍長達數百英哩 , 進入太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	而當我們將這個圖片上色 , 帶出微弱的光線 , 我們看到這些噴射流進行反射 , 事實上 , 我們看到在其它的圖像中 , 噴射流的距離比土衛二上數千英哩 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和團隊檢查了像這樣的圖像 , 思考了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們的結論是 , 這些噴流可能從土衛二地表下的液態水噴出 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過剩的熱量 。
