in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們很有可能偶然發現現代行星探索的聖杯 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合生命有機生命體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其他地方發現生命 , 無論是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明在我們的太陽系中 , 創世紀就不只發生過一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立發生在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 根據推理說 , 在宇宙中它已經發生了非常驚人的次數 , 以及137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是我們所知唯一還有生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 它依然是我們唯一的家園 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座的哪位1960年代的時候頭腦還靈活--我們原諒你們 , 如果不是 , 還好你們還記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球從太空中被拍攝到 , 它對於我們在宇宙中的定位有著極大的影響 , 以及我們對於保護地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們卡西尼號拍下了相當於首張照片 , 一張從來沒有人看過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全食的日偏食 , 從土星的另一端看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無與倫比的照片中 , 看到背光時的主光環 , 看到太陽折射後的形象 , 還看到由土衛二表面噴出的光環 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們就能在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 看見了我們自己的星球 , 還藏在土星光環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 關於從遠處觀看我們自己有種深入人心的觀點 , 並捕捉到我們天空中小小的、藍色的星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 和我們從中得到的自我的觀點 , 可能就是在半個世紀前 , 我們從這個探索之旅得到的最佳回報 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到了2005年 , 只剩下15%的世界在災難過後進行補助 , 隱藏了未使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短短的演講中 , 谷歌的lalitekatrada的demoda地圖製作者 , 全球各地的人用製圖工具來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 獨眼巨人摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	幾百萬人急需救助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人力物力和物資交給該地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但是沒有標示道路的地圖標示醫院的地圖也沒有可以幫助到氣旋受害者
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區對應到可數位化的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國跟世界大部分人口所面臨的問題沒有詳細的地圖
but help was coming .	但救援要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google有40位志願者使用了一套新軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 物流及救援中心
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個能夠授權我們每個人的科技 , 讓我們在當地繪製我們已知的東西 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們使用這套軟體標註道路 , 河流 , 從學校 , 到當地企業 , 錄影店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎被提名人hernandodestoto看出 , 大部分開發中國家要用經濟升級的關鍵 , 就是要去觸及大量未清除的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 光在印度就有價值一兆美金的房地產保持不住
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年170個國家數以千計的使用者就標註了數以百萬計的資訊 , 並創造了一張地圖 , 顯示出的細節是前所未有的 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這是因為各地熱情的使用者的力量所實現的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看一些目前使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們說話的同時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們在繪製世界上的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑剛為塞內加爾標註了路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離這裡近一點 , 夏盧亞 , 班加羅爾的n.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學、姿勢辨識以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數百個城市裡的數千個使用者的勝利一個使用者一次編輯一筆資訊
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是對70%的未開發星球的一個邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦的巴勒斯坦村莊布德魯斯進行了十個月的非暴力抗爭 , 阻止他們在橄欖枝節上進行一場障礙 。 你聽過了嗎 ? 也不這麼想 。 巴西的製片家朱利亞•巴查問過 , 為什麼我們只關注以色列抗爭中的暴力 , 而非暴力領袖有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞•巴夏:注意非暴力事件 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列與巴勒斯坦人的作品他們試圖用和平手段結束衝突
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我跟我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總會想出一個問題:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面對的挑戰是 , 通常我才剛從中東回來 , 我在那裡拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力手段來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人致力於推動一個巨大的國家非暴力運動來結束這次佔領並建立地區的和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂 , 介於發生在地面上的狀況 , 和對國外的感知之間的分歧 , 正是其中一個關鍵的原因 , 說明了我們尚未能成功做到巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我在這裡就是要談關注的力量、關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩及其他地方的興起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力要成長的大部分 , 並不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要讓我們開始去注意那些本來就已經是的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	請允許我帶你到這個名為布德魯斯的村子來闡明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨了滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈要築起分隔的障礙 , 一部分的障礙會建在村莊上面 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並且被包圍住如此便無法自由往返約旦河西岸的其他地區
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領袖啟發 , 他們發動了一場和平抗爭活動 , 阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以看出到底是怎麼一回事 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會分隔巴勒斯坦和以色列
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村我們發現這道牆將竊取我們的土地
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:這柵欄事實上創造了恐怖的解答
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你的身邊是數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:軍隊害怕的比非暴力反對者
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看見男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空腦中的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是在完全和諧的 , 我們想要將它傳播給全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯、及流行界線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍籬的衝突持續著
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來驅散群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的武力
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是實彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像費魯吉亞一樣 。 到處拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我相信我們都會死去 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊 , 還有一些人甚至不合作 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭是無法阻止其發展的 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱麗亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一連串驚人的事件而這不過就發生在七年前 , 在2003年
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地上移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的以色列與巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍整個西岸的村子以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦人居住的地區
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體還是維持著這些故事的大部分時間
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種寂靜對非暴力的可能性有著深遠的影響 , 甚至會在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共同點它們都是劇院中的一種形式在尋求他們的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有使用暴力的人才能上頭版並引起國際對於巴勒斯坦議題的關注變得很難讓非暴力組織領袖為他們的社區所做的報告說明公民抗命是個可行的選項來處理他們的困境
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能會對在場的父母也不會感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子丟出越來越大聲的脾氣 , 最好的方法就是在他第一次丟出去時給予他注意 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	這種吵鬧的行為 , 會變成兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母只要把注意力交給他們的孩子 , 就可以鼓勵或抑制這樣的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可能會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東地區的衝突的核心上 , 帶動和平是要我們把非暴力行為轉變成一個功能性行為 , 做法是讓更多的注意到現今的非暴力領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝約旦河西岸的村子加薩地區以及東耶路撒冷的村子時 , 我見識到就算只是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在瓦拉杰村 , 靠近耶路撒冷的一個村子裡 , 整個社區面臨和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 且無法自由進入 , 不論是約旦河西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力運動兩年了 , 但因為沒有人注意到他們 , 已經被放棄了 。
so we organized a screening .	於是我們安排了一個篩選方式 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了至今為止人數最多也最有紀律的展示 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	主辦人說村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在一部電影裡 , 感覺到確實有人在跟隨他們所做的事情 , 人們在乎
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續向前 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這邊 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做solidariot , 在希伯來語中意思是團結一致 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這場運動的領導人已經把布德鲁斯村當作主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們回報以色列人從來沒有活動過 , 在看電影時 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 也開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰族和索利達里德拉格運動的例子顯示 , 即使只是一小部份的獨立製片也能將非暴力行為轉化為功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大型媒體遊客可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導在村落發生的非暴力抗爭 , 比如bil、ni'lin、瓦拉杰 , 在耶路撒冷的街坊中 , 如謝赫賈拉和silwan , 非暴力領袖在他們的作品中會變得更加明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要理解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像它們從未發生一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見過 , 如果我們有 , 他們會繁衍下去 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會成長在以色列與巴勒斯坦的衝突中 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於可以解開這情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的 , 在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	我們來關注他們 , 讓他們能夠證明在任何地方都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•薩克有一個簡單但強大的領導模式 , 都是從金色圈子開始 , 及 「 為什麼 」 這個問題 。 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金、和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導能力 , 銷售 , 成功
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•朗克:偉大領袖如何激勵大家行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你如何解釋當事情不如我們所設想的一般 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠做到似乎違反所有假設的事情時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 它們的創新性高於所有的競爭 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有同樣的才華的管道、同樣的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德金恩領導黑人民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到迫害的人他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能想辦法控制飛行器 ? 為什麼有其他團隊更有資格、更有資格......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達到發動人飛行的效果 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他的 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 它甚至深深改變了我以它為運作方式的觀點 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大而具啟發性的領導者和機構不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金恩或他們所有人都以同樣的方式思考、行動與溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且跟其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼過來 , 而這可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 怎麼做 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領袖能夠激發其他人不去的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這些詞彙 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上的每一個人、每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百肯定 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何做到的 , 不論你稱之為你不同的價值主張、你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但非常非常少數的人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我說的 「 為什麼 」 不是指 「 為了賺取利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 一直都是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的起因是什麼 ? 你的信仰是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎呢 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們的思考方式我們的行為與溝通方式都是由外而內的
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚到最模糊不清的
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但是這些受啟發的領導者和那些受啟發的機構不管它們的規模 , 不管它們的產業都以由內而外的方式去思考、行動與溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易懂 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 它們發出的推銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們都設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 用途也很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」 「 梅 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	那就是我們大多數人溝通的方式
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數的銷售也就是多數人互相通訊的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何比較好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶服務 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的汽油里程 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果電腦實際上溝通的方式是
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信都在挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 設計得很簡單 , 使用者也很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你們準備好從我這裡買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是扭轉了資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它證明了我們 , 人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們會買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一位都對買蘋果電腦感到相當自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常安心 , 要從蘋果買一台mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但是 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	在結構上 , 沒有什麼能夠區別它們的競爭對手 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都有資格做這些產品
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面螢幕電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製造平面螢幕電視
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面螢幕監視多年了 ,
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦推出mp3播放器跟pda , 他們製作出很棒的品質產品 , 而且他們可以製作出完美設計過的產品 , 而且沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要向一家電腦公司購買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是與每個需要你有什麼的人在做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目的是要跟那些相信你所相信的人們做生意
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	以下是最棒的部分:我告訴你們的都不是我個人的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都深植在生物學的信條裡 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 是生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你觀察人腦的橫斷圖從上往下看你會看到人腦實際上分裂成三個主要的組成和黃金圈完美地相關
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的腦 , 人類的大腦 , 我們的大腦皮層 , 與 「 什麼 」 的層次對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法以及語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個區塊組成了我們的邊緣腦 , 我們的邊緣腦是負責所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為、所有決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特色、好處、事實 , 和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它無法驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能由內而外溝通時 , 我們就在對著控制行為的腦部直接對話 , 然後我們允許人們去合理化它 , 用我們說且有形的事情去做 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是我們用膽識做決定的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會把事實和數字給別人 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是什麼 , 但就是感覺不太對勁 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 不用 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為管控決策的腦並不控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	而我們最多能整理出的是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺就是不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時候你說你帶著你的心臟 , 或者你帶著你的靈魂走出來 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	我很不想對你說 , 那些都不是身體的其他部份在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	都是發生在你邊緣的腦裡 , 是控制決策而非語言的部份 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做你該做的事 , 而人們對為什麼你做你該做的事有何反應 , 那麼你怎麼會得到別人來投票給你、購買你有什麼 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 要忠實並且想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不只是賣給需要你東西的人 , 目標是賣東西給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 還要僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人僅是因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為了你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會為你工作 , 用血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	而在20世紀初追尋人類飛行就像當時的網路公司一樣
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的 , 是成功的關鍵
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問別人: 「 為什麼你的產品或公司會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	而人們總會給你相同的三件事:不合時宜、不對勁的人、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是這三樣東西 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley因戰爭部門捐贈了5萬美金去想出這個飛行機器
money was no problem .	金錢是沒問題的 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛任職於斯密森學院 , 工作得非常順暢 ; 他認識當時的所有大型腦袋 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的人才資金來源而且市場狀況超讚
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都為langley加油 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們怎麼會從沒聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠在俄亥俄州、奧維爾和威爾伯萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用腳踏車店裡的現金來支付夢想 , 沒有任何一個人在萊特兄弟的團隊受過大學教育 , 連奧維爾或威爾伯都沒有 ; 《紐約時報》緊隨其後 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 奧維爾和威爾伯是出於某種目的而驅使的 , 出於一種信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器這將改變世界的軌道
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人的時候 ,
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗與淚水和他們一同努力工作的人
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外一些人則是為了錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	而他們會說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出門他們都會帶五套零件 , 因為這是他們來吃飯前會墜機的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛了甚至沒有人去體驗它
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley因為錯誤的動機在萊特兄弟起飛那天 , 離職了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會在你們的科技上不斷進步 。 」 但他並沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢他沒有變有名 , 所以放棄 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信什麼 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂 「 創新法則 」 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你一定會知道它的術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口中前2.5%的人是創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期使用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數晚期的大多數以及落後者
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式電話的唯一原因是因為你再也買不到輪子手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	在這個尺度上 , 我們都坐在不同的位置 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功 , 或是大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你不可能擁有它 , 除非你在15%到18%之間的市場占有率的引爆點 , 然後系統就會開始倒退 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很愛告訴你: 「 喔 , 值得驕傲吧 。 大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以絆超過10%的顧客 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 了解 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是有本能的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:在你做生意之前 , 你要如何找到那些在你做生意之前就拿到的而不是那些拿不到的人呢 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 就是這個 , 這個小小的差距 , 你必須要結束 , 如同jeffreymoore稱它為: 「 跨越鴻溝 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的多數人不會嘗試直到其他人已經先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 這些發明家以及早期的採用者他們對做這些膽試的決定感到很自在
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更為自在也就是由他們所相信的世界所帶動而非只是可得的產品
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六個小時買剛上市iphone的人 , 在下個星期你剛剛可以走進店裡 , 然後在店裡買了一個下來 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花40 , 000美金在平版電視剛上市的人雖然這項技術還未被更新
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們這麼做並不因為這項技術很棒他們這麼做是為了他們自己
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想成為第一名
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅證明了你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	這個人在前六小時買iphone的原因 , 排隊排了六個小時 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們想要每個人如何看他們:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說 , 成功的祕訣是金錢、對的人和對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo推出的八、九年前到現今這一天 , 他們是這市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下一人 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金都極為豐足
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件真的很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當做動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我常常會在我的垃圾時報dvr上的小東西上
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但是tivo卻失敗了
they've never made money .	他們從沒賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們上ipos的時候 , 他們的股票價格是30到40美金 , 然後一跌到底 , 從來沒有在10以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為這甚至超過6項以上交易除了幾項小漲幅
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們擁有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一項產品可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 重播現場的電視節目 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 而不是你問的 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	那些憤世嫉俗的人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 也不喜歡它
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控自己生活的每一方面 , 孩子 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場節目 , 跳過商業廣告 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子有關創意的散播法則
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函而當時也沒有網站去查看日期
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是在美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到迫害的人在美國公民權普及前的時代
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的想法有一些很糟
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他並沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	" 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , " 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的 , 相信他所相信的 , 相信他所相信的 , 相信他所相信的 , 相信他所相信的 , 相信他所相信的 , 奪去他的理想
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個字傳達給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	大家看 , 有25萬人在對的時機出現在對的時間 , 去聽他的演講 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	是他們所相信的美國使他們踏上公車8小時的路程 , 以在八月中時站在華盛頓的太陽下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	那是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑與白:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種不同的法律:那些是由更高權威的人所定的法律 , 以及那些由人類所定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有法律都和高權威制定的法律一致否則我們將生活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動是幫助他終身的最佳方式 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便一提 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計劃 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在請聽政治人物 , 用他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導人 , 有領導者 , 有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但是那些領導的人啟發了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	無論是個人或組織我們跟隨那些領導的人不是因為我們必須而是因為我們想要
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	而正是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開頭的人 , 有能力去啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到那些啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你如何記住你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你如何知道你是正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家以研究我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何與記憶、想像力連結 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•布瑞奇斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你的位置 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們把車停在一個很大的停車場 , 我們怎麼記住我們停的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬所面對的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以我們從海馬體開始 , 以黃色顯示 , 它是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒受到損害 , 像在阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住事情 , 包括你把車子停哪 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是以拉丁文 「 海馬 」 取名 , 它的名字是 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像其餘的腦一樣 , 它是由神經元所構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類的腦內有大約一千億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元間藉由神經元間的連結互相傳遞脈衝或發送電突波
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬迴是由兩片細胞組成的 , 它們緊密相連 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶的運作方式 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠在覓食時的個別神經元 , 或探索尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們要想像我們紀錄一個單個神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體裡面
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一點電流時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到這個神經元知道老鼠在環境中的某個特定位置
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	並藉由電的突波來傳遞訊號給大腦 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以把神經元發射的速度呈現為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄很多不同的神經元我們會發現當動物到其它地方時不同神經元會被激發像是這個方形的盒子
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們會在腦中其他地方建立一張地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人體內
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時候需要腦部監控的腦部活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在一個小鎮中開車閒晃
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	河馬體內的位置細胞就會發出資訊 , 活躍起來 , 開始傳送電脈衝 , 每當他們開車經過那個小鎮的某個特定地點 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠在環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這裡的兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界特別重要
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以上面那隻喜歡在老鼠的牆壁中間發射光芒 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你把盒子的位置再擴大時 ,
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	當南方靠近一面牆壁時 , 下面的那個就會被激發 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放進另一道牆那細胞在這兩個地方都會被激發當動物隨意在箱子裡頭探索時在南邊有一道牆
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測了感覺你周圍的邊界線的距離和方向──延伸的建築物等等──對海馬體是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在被海馬體輸入的訊息上 , 細胞會被投射到海馬體裡面 , 海馬體的確可以準確地偵測到範圍或邊緣 , 在特定的距離和方向 , 由老鼠或老鼠四處探索 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以在左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆時 , 會被激發 , 或向東邊的界線 , 不論是邊緣的 , 或方形的牆壁 , 或圓形的圓形牆壁 , 或甚至是桌子邊緣的一滴 , 那些動物跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞當邊緣到南邊時會被激發不管是在邊緣還是邊緣的還是牆壁或甚至兩張桌子間的縫隙
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	以上是我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物所在的何處 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以檢驗我們認為物體的位置 , 例如這一目標旗桿 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或是你的車子的位置 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把牠們放回環境中 , 一般來說牠們很擅長在牠們認為旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以了解他們認為旗幟位置的改變 , 如何改變形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉個例子 , 你看到的旗子在方形的環境中 , 如果問人們身在何處 , 讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟的位置會被延伸出去 , 就像位置細胞被激發出去一樣 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由將圖案儲存在你所在位置細胞的位置 , 然後你可以藉由四處移動回到那個位置 , 將現行的位置與你所在位置細胞被激發的模式與那儲存模式相吻合 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們是從動作來的 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們走一些下限的路徑──也許我們會停車 , 脫掉我們所知道的──因為我們自己的動作 , 可以整合這條路 , 大致上回到前端的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一種叫做 「 網格細胞 」 的細胞輸入到這種路徑 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞也是在海馬迴的輸入信號上發現它們有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但 , 當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞會激發一系列不同的位置 , 分佈在環境各處 , 形成一個非常規律的三角形網格 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄數個網格細胞的資料 , 在這裡以不同的顏色標記 , 每個細胞的網格激發模式 , 會和其他細胞相比 , 稍微偏移 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以紅色的在這個網格被激發而綠色的在這個 , 藍色的在這個 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 就好像這隻老鼠可以在自己的環境內放入一個虛擬空間的網格有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和經度線條但用的是三角形的網格
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它所在的位置 , 讓它可以使用它自己的動作 , 來知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有網格激發的模式有著相同的對稱軸突 , 同一個軸對稱 , 在這裡以橙色標記 , 這意味著在特定的腦部區域中 , 所有網格細胞的活動 , 應該根據我們是否在六個方向跑步 , 或在六個方向跑步 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放到磁共振成像掃描儀中 , 讓他們做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛給你們看的電玩遊戲 , 並尋找這訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人腦內的 「 連體皮質 」 裡也看得到它 , 就跟你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得車子的位置和方向在他停車位的位置和邊界
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這可以藉由邊界偵測細胞來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也在記住他走出車子停車場的路徑 , 這可以用網格細胞激發的模式來呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動找到他當初車子停放的位置 , 來找出哪個位置和目前他大腦中停車位置細胞的激發模式與目前停車位的儲存模式相吻合 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那會引導他回到那個位置 , 不尊重視視覺提示 , 比如他的車是否真的在那 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許是已傳來的
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道去那裡取得它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們觀察整個大腦內的網格狀激發模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置上看到 , 當我們進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是處在活躍狀態 , 比如 , 記住你上次參加婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能神經機制來呈現在我們四周的空間 , 也用在產生視覺影像 , 讓我們可以重建出空間的景象 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	如果這是發生的 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始互相活化 , 透過這些高密度的相互連結 , 然後再重新活化邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這種視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一個類型的細胞 , 頭向細胞 , 我還沒提過 , 它們會像指南針一樣根據你的面向來發射 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從這裡定義你的視覺角度 , 為你的視覺影像產生一個影像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上 , 會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個認知神經科學領域的新時代的例子 , 認知神經科學正開始了解心理的過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是以十億個單獨神經元的行為來思考 , 構成我們的大腦 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像全球安全是由各機構、政府、私營部門 , 及公共機構共同驅動的 。 這不僅僅是距離開源粉絲的遠景 , 也是南大西洋公共電視台的最高指揮官 , 北大西洋公約組織擁有來自近期軍事歷史的生動時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全 , 應該用橋樑來建造 , 而不是靠牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題開源、和平、政治、社群媒體暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特里迪斯:北大西洋的最高統帥 , 如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要來談談開放式安全性 , 因為我們在這21世紀 , 必須要做得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說說 , 我們先回顧二十世紀吧 , 來了解安全這個風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在verdun , 1916年 , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人死亡 , 所以每天大約兩千人被殺 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它向前推進20世紀的安全轉為二次世界大戰你會看到史達林格的戰鬥 , 300天 , 兩百萬人被殺
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬其頓防線 , 然後進入冷戰時期 , 鐵幕 , 柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的主題是 , 與其建造圍牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它就在drina河上 , 是作家伊沃安德里的小說的主題 , 它談到在歐洲和巴爾幹半島中 , 那些非常困擾的部分 , 經過一段時間 , 有非常多建牆的牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 毫不猶豫地 , 要團結在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我想再次重申 , 開放式安全是關于國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的和公共的 , 並且通過戰略性交流 , 大致上在社交網路上聯系在一起 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要那樣做 , 因為我們的全球公有物被攻擊在各種層面下 , 且對於全球公有物的威脅都不會被用來建造牆壁來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條繩子 , 穿過印度洋 ,
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	沿著整個音樂廳的鐵絲網
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	就是為了防止海盜攻擊
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是當今世界各地都非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬斯加的海峽很活躍
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	在幾內亞灣活躍
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球交通系統中 , 價值一百億年的不連續性 ,
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500名船員被綁架 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何去處理
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	咱們轉到另一種海洋 , 網絡海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩位年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁著 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們進行了一項信用卡詐欺 , 網絡超過一百億美元 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分它是全球經濟的二兆年不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	兩萬億的一年 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這僅僅是在英國的國內生產總值之下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這種網絡大海 , 我們知道無止盡的是激進開放的基礎 , 正在受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我在全球公有物中所擔心的另一件事 , 是人口販賣所帶來的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片等行動 , 由從阿富汗穿過歐洲到達美國的這一波的威脅 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部運過來的可卡因
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸問題 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人力的運輸 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要是在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我真希望我能告訴你這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍武器用來阻止販賣人口販子 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個販毒集團的半潛水的設備 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美的叢林裡建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏逮捕了它 , 它正運載著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 , 精良的通訊橫掃了
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣行為 , 在人身上、在人身上、在武器、被禁止、在大規模毀滅性武器中 , 都是被威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	一起在今天的阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是在阿富汗的一個花田
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界80%到90%的小便、鴉片和海洛因從阿富汗出來 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們當然也看到了恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是基地組織的發源地 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個很強烈的暴亂就嵌在了那裡 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須去處理的事 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 在21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們20世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼辦 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不能僅僅依靠槍支來提供安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不能僅僅依靠槍支 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做的時候 , 我們必須做得很好 , 而且要能幹 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人和公共的聯繫 , 由網路上的戰略溝通的概念所拉出的 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這是如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 , 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書本 ,
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說 , " 這太奇怪了 , 我想我讀到這個在二十幾、三十幾歲的年輕男女 , 很大程度上在阿富汗不識字 。 "
you would be correct .	你會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%的人進入安全部隊時是無法閱讀的 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些男人和女人要學會閱讀的時期 , 就能接受塔利班的教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裏 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀 , 透過北大西洋的課程 , 與私人機構合作 , 與發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教了超過二十萬的阿富汗安全部隊士兵去讀和寫作基本上 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你能在阿富汗讀寫你通常會在口袋裏放一支筆
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在儀式上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們很驕傲的拿出筆 , 放在他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這就把國際聯合起來 , 有五十個國家涉及這個任務 , 跨部門和這些發展機構 , 還有私人和公共機構 , 一起進行這類安全的考量 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教他們戰鬥技能 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著連接上能夠創造更持久的安全效應的方式 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	叫做comfort號 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船 , 名為mercy號 ,
they are hospital ships .	他們是一艘醫院船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的運作穿過加勒比海和南美洲的海岸 , 進行病人的治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	通常 , 他們會進行40萬個病人的治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它是由船員們 , 並非嚴格地從軍 , 而是人道組織結合:行動希望、專案微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織送來志願者
interagency physicians come out .	跨年齡的醫師出來
they're all part of this .	他們都是這方面的一部份 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子來說明這個撞擊的影響力 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 和他的母親走了兩天來到安慰號上的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被安置在極度神秘的眼神裡 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo. 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界了 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將這個乘以40萬個病人治療的心血 , 這個私人和公共的合作關係 , 和安全的力量一起合作 , 然後你會開始發現以截然不同的方式創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手

they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位年輕男孩的一邊的年輕人 。 這是棒球診所的一部分 , 我們曾經探索過大聯盟棒球聯盟 , 國務院 , 設立了這支球隊的外交部 , 軍隊棒球隊的選手們 , 他們是真正的軍人 , 但他們參與了這個任務 , 他們在拉丁美洲和加勒比地區 , 和加勒比地區 , 開到了全美洲和加勒比的棒球聯盟 , 開到了全國棒球 , 開到了全美洲和加 , 開到了安巴拉斯 , 開到了第七棒球場 , 開到了北部 , 開到了北部 , 開到了全美洲 , 開到了北部 , 開到了第七個球隊 , 開到了第四個球隊 , 開到了美國 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它給年輕人看的典範 , 展現出健身和生活的榜樣 , 而我認為這幫助我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這個合作夥伴的另一面是災難救援中 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍的直升機 , 參與於2004年的海嘯之後 , 殺死了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大災難中-2004年的海嘯、25萬人死亡 , 2005年的巴基斯坦地震、8萬5千人死亡 , 海地地地震 , 大約30萬人死亡 , 更近期是發生在日本的地震海嘯 , 震驚了日本和其核工業 。 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際間的合作 , 跨部門的合作 , 和公民安全部門之間的合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些都是開放式安全觀念的例子 。

i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表一個像這樣的演講 。 我說 , 我對你們說 , 我在facebook上 , 朋友 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾的笑聲 ,
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	曾經有一篇文章由ap , 在鋼索上運行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	被帶到世界上兩個地方:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北約司令需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是催化劑 , 隔天早上我就有數百個臉書好友請求 , 來自印尼人和芬蘭人 , 大多會說: 「 司令 , 我們聽說你需要朋友 , 喔 , 順便一提 , 北約有什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們移動訊息的方式 , 傳遞訊息是我們如何連結國際 , 跨部門 , 公私的和這些社群網路 , 以協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我再提個嚴肅的話題 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這張照片是一位勇敢的英國士兵 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭警衛隊
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在赫爾曼的手錶 , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我把他放到這裡來提醒我們 , 我不想讓任何人離開房間 , 只想著我們不需要有能力 , 具有能力的軍事力量 , 就可以創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這是我們是誰及我們做了什麼的核心 , 我們為了保護自由 , 言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍藏的事情 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 人生並不是開機 ,
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有一支軍隊要不是在戰爭中 , 就是在營房裡 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會說 , 人生是個風雲人物 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你得要調一下話題 , 想想在21世紀 , 我們要如何創造安全 , 會有時候 , 我們會在真正的戰爭和危機中使用硬實力 , 但會有很多時候 , 如同我們今天談到的 , 我們的軍隊會是21世紀安全的一部分 , 國際的 , 跨部門 , 公私結合 , 和有能力溝通的一部分 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	我想說今天早些時候 , 我們都聽說過維基百科 。 我經常用維基百科查一些事實 , 你們都明白 , 維基百科並不是由12個聰明的人所創造而來 , 寫一些文章 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有成千上萬的人在輸入資訊 , 每天有數百萬人在提取那些資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這完美的畫面能展現基礎 , 沒有人能像大家一起思考一樣聰明 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個人比我們所有人一起思考時 , 一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基的願景陳述非常簡單:一個人類可以自由共享所有知識的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我給你們的論點是 , 通過結合國際 , 跨部門 , 公私力量 , 戰略通信 , 加上這21世紀 , 我們就能創造出所有安全的總和 。
